Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
The First Absurdity: Incapacitating God
Nasafi proves that granting creative power to creatures leads to incapacitating God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how granting a creature independent creative power logically leads to the impossibility of God being incapacitated.

Core Idea
A creature's free choice cannot be allowed to override God's power.

This passage is the first of three absurdities that Nasafi derives from the Ash'ari doctrine of acquiring (kasb) or attributing creative power to creatures. He constructs a reductio argument: if a creature could independently create an act, then God's power to create the opposite would depend on the creature's choice not to act. This would make God's power contingent on a creature, which is impossible. The argument hinges on the incompatibility of opposites.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
God wills to create movement in a creature's hand, and the creature wills to create stillness in the same hand. Note that these are opposites.
Opposites cannot coexist in the same locus at the same time.
2
Recognize the impossibility of coexistence
Since movement and stillness are opposites, they cannot both be actualized. Only one can exist.
3
See the dependence on the creature's choice
For God's movement to be realized, the creature must refrain from creating stillness. This makes God's power conditional upon the creature's choice.
4
Realize the implication: incapacitation
The creature is free to choose; if he chooses to create stillness, God's power is thwarted. This means the creature can remove God's power, which is incapacitation (ta'jiz) or prevention (man'), both impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونبين كيفية كون كل من ذلك مؤديا إلى كل وجه من هذه الوجوه بعون الله وتوفيقه. أما الأول فإنا قلنا: إن ذلك يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري جل وعلا فإن الباري لو كان قادرا على أن يخلق مثلا في يد العبد حركة، والعبد قادر على أن يخلق فيه سكونا ثم من المحال أن يوجد مقدور كل واحد منهما في المحل في وقت واحد لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال. فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه. قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلا عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة على المتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار ومن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن اختيار.
We will explain how each of these leads to each of these aspects with the help of God and His success. As for the first, we said: That leads to incapacitating the Creator, Glorious and Exalted. For if the Creator were able to create, for example, a movement in the hand of the servant, and the servant were able to create a stillness in it, then it is impossible for the object of power of each of them to exist in the locus at one time due to the opposition between movement and stillness – and there is no dispute about this with a rational person. When this is the case, then the establishment of God’s power over His object of power becomes dependent on the servant’s refraining from achieving his object of power. And if he did not refrain from achieving his object of power, then God’s power over His object of power would not be established – thus God’s power over His object of power is conditioned upon the servant’s refraining from achieving his own object of power. And the servant, in refraining from achieving his object of power, is a free chooser: if he wills he refrains, and if he wills he does not refrain. So he becomes a chooser in removing God’s power: if he wills he removes it from His object of power, and if he wills he does not remove it. And removing power is incapacitation according to us, and according to you it is prevention due to the permissibility of combining power with prevention according to you; and both matters – I mean prevention or incapacitation – are impossible. If they say: We charge you that on this [view] the Creator would not be powerful over opposites, because if He were powerful over them and then brought one of the opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and would prevent Himself from achieving what opposes it due to the impossibility of opposites subsisting in a locus; and just as it is not permissible for the Creator to be prevented or incapacitated by someone else, it is not permissible for Him to be prevented or incapacitated by Himself. It is said: Indeed, God is powerful over each of the opposites on an alternating basis (ʿalā al-badal); thus He is described as being able to bring about stillness in this locus in this state instead of the movement He brought about in it, and likewise for reversal. And He is not described as having power over opposites absolutely, because their combination is impossible, and the impossible does not enter under power. And by this, His power over His object of power was not attached to the choice of another. Rather, He is powerful to do whichever of the opposites He wills, and whichever of the opposites He creates, He creates by choice; and whichever He refrains from, He refrains from by choice.
Source pages p. 882

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument demonstrating the first absurdity: that ascribing creative power to a creature leads to incapacitating God. The author begins by stating the claim and then constructs a reductio argument. He supposes God wills to create movement in a hand, and a servant wills to create stillness in the same hand. Since movement and stillness are opposites, they cannot coexist. Therefore, God's power to create movement depends on the servant not creating stillness. But the servant is free to choose whether to refrain; if he chooses not to refrain, God's power fails. This would mean the servant can remove God's power, which is either ta'jīz (incapacitation) or man' (prevention) – both impossible. The author then addresses an objection: the opponent argues that on this reasoning, God would not be able to create opposites, because if He creates one He prevents Himself from the other. The answer is that God's power over opposites is on an alternating basis (badal); He can create one or the other, but not both simultaneously. Thus His power is not dependent on a creature's choice; rather, He freely chooses which opposite to create. The impossible (simultaneous opposites) is not an object of power. This preserves God's absolute power and independence.

Key Terms
تعجيز
منع
مضادان
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power and creature's power can operate on different aspects without conflict, so no incapacitation occurs.
Correction: The argument shows that if both powers are over the same specific act (e.g., stillness in the hand), they directly compete. The creature's power would directly oppose God's intended act, leading to incapacitation.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's argument, what is the consequence of the creature's freedom to choose?
A) God's power is unaffected by the creature's choice
B) God's power becomes dependent on the creature's choice
C) The creature cannot create opposites because of God's power
D) Both God and creature can create simultaneously

Key Takeaway
Granting independent creative power to a creature leads to the absurd conclusion that God's power can be overridden by a creature's free choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin or fail to obey Allah, do you ever feel that your will has 'overpowered' His command? How does this passage dismantle that feeling and what should your response be instead?
?
Are there areas of your life where you live as if your choices are independent of Allah's will and power? What would change if you truly believed that every action of yours is entirely within Allah's control and that He is never made incapable by your decisions?
?
This lesson argues that no creature can thwart Allah's power. Does your heart truly rest in that certainty, or do you sometimes fear that your own weakness or the actions of others can frustrate Allah's plan? Repent of any such doubt and affirm Tawheed.

Responding to the Objection: God's Power Over Opposites on an Alternating Basis
Nasafi answers the objection that God would be incapacitated if He cannot create opposites together.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi responds to the objection that God would be incapacitated if He cannot create opposites simultaneously, by explaining His power is on an alternating basis (badal).

Core Idea
God's power over opposites is not simultaneous but successive, preserving His absolute freedom.

Having argued that granting creatures creative power leads to incapacitating God, Nasafi anticipates an objection: opponents might argue that on his own reasoning, God would be unable to create opposites at the same time, implying a limitation. Nasafi responds by clarifying that God's power is over each opposite on an alternating basis (badal). He can create one or the other, but not both simultaneously, because the impossible is not an object of power. This response reaffirms God's sovereignty and independence from any creature's choice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The opponent argues that if God cannot create two opposites simultaneously, then He is either incapacitated or prevents Himself – similar to the earlier argument.
2
Recognize the key distinction: badal (alternation)
Nasafi states that God is powerful over each opposite on a badal basis – He can create one instead of the other, not both together.
This is not a limitation; it's the nature of power over logical opposites.
3
Realize that impossibility is not an object of power
The simultaneous existence of opposites is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power.
4
Conclude that God's power is not dependent on creatures
God freely chooses which opposite to create; His power is not attached to the choice of another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونبين كيفية كون كل من ذلك مؤديا إلى كل وجه من هذه الوجوه بعون الله وتوفيقه. أما الأول فإنا قلنا: إن ذلك يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري جل وعلا فإن الباري لو كان قادرا على أن يخلق مثلا في يد العبد حركة، والعبد قادر على أن يخلق فيه سكونا ثم من المحال أن يوجد مقدور كل واحد منهما في المحل في وقت واحد لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال. فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه. قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلا عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة على المتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار ومن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن اختيار.
We will explain how each of these leads to each of these aspects with the help of God and His success. As for the first, we said: That leads to incapacitating the Creator, Glorious and Exalted. For if the Creator were able to create, for example, a movement in the hand of the servant, and the servant were able to create a stillness in it, then it is impossible for the object of power of each of them to exist in the locus at one time due to the opposition between movement and stillness – and there is no dispute about this with a rational person. When this is the case, then the establishment of God’s power over His object of power becomes dependent on the servant’s refraining from achieving his object of power. And if he did not refrain from achieving his object of power, then God’s power over His object of power would not be established – thus God’s power over His object of power is conditioned upon the servant’s refraining from achieving his own object of power. And the servant, in refraining from achieving his object of power, is a free chooser: if he wills he refrains, and if he wills he does not refrain. So he becomes a chooser in removing God’s power: if he wills he removes it from His object of power, and if he wills he does not remove it. And removing power is incapacitation according to us, and according to you it is prevention due to the permissibility of combining power with prevention according to you; and both matters – I mean prevention or incapacitation – are impossible. If they say: We charge you that on this [view] the Creator would not be powerful over opposites, because if He were powerful over them and then brought one of the opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and would prevent Himself from achieving what opposes it due to the impossibility of opposites subsisting in a locus; and just as it is not permissible for the Creator to be prevented or incapacitated by someone else, it is not permissible for Him to be prevented or incapacitated by Himself. Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument demonstrating the first absurdity: that ascribing creative power to a creature leads to incapacitating God. The author begins by stating the claim and then constructs a reductio argument. He supposes God wills to create movement in a hand, and a servant wills to create stillness in the same hand. Since movement and stillness are opposites, they cannot coexist. Therefore, God's power to create movement depends on the servant not creating stillness. But the servant is free to choose whether to refrain; if he chooses not to refrain, God's power fails. This would mean the servant can remove God's power, which is either ta'jīz (incapacitation) or man' (prevention) – both impossible. The author then addresses an objection: the opponent argues that on this reasoning, God would not be able to create opposites, because if He creates one He prevents Himself from the other. The answer is that God's power over opposites is on an alternating basis (badal); He can create one or the other, but not both simultaneously. Thus His power is not dependent on a creature's choice; rather, He freely chooses which opposite to create. The impossible (simultaneous opposites) is not an object of power. This preserves God's absolute power and independence.

Key Terms
قدرة على البدل
المحال
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God cannot create both opposites simultaneously, then His power is limited.
Correction: Nasafi explains that power over the impossible (simultaneous opposites) is not a real limitation; the impossible is inherently non-existent, so it is not an object of power. God's power is complete over all possible things.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's response, on what basis is God powerful over opposites?
A) Simultaneously
B) On an alternating basis (badal)
C) Not at all
D) Only over one opposite

Key Takeaway
God's power over opposites is on an alternating basis; He freely chooses which opposite to create, and His power is not dependent on any creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where it seems God's power is limited (e.g., evil, unanswered prayer), do you really trust that His inability to create impossible things is a sign of His perfection, not weakness? How does the idea of 'power on an alternating basis' change your confidence in His ultimate control?
?
This lesson says God's power is not attached to any creature's choice. In what area of your life have you been acting as if your choices force God's hand—where you need to repent and acknowledge His absolute freedom to choose?
?
Do you ever resent that God doesn't give you both options (e.g., health and wealth, comfort and challenge) at once? How does understanding that He chooses one opposite at a time, by His perfect wisdom, help you submit to His will today?

Divine Attributes

The Impossibility of God's Power Depending on Human Choice
Al-Nasafi argues that dependency on human choice leads to impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that if God's power over an object depended on the servant's refraining from acquiring that object, it would lead to an impossibility (disabling or prevention).

Core Idea
God's power cannot be made dependent on human choice; that would be impossible.

Al-Nasafi begins by setting up a logical problem for those who claim that human acquisition (kasb) implies that God's power over an object depends on the servant refraining from creating that object. He argues that this leads to a vicious circle where the servant's choice can remove God's power, which is impossible. Let's examine this argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Start with the undeniable opposition between motion and rest. This is common knowledge.
2
Follow the conditional
If God's power over an object depended on the servant refraining from acquiring that object, then the servant's choice would determine whether God's power is established.
3
Identify the two consequences
Al-Nasafi says that according to the opponent, removing power is either disabling (ta'jiz) or prevention (man'). Both are impossible.
Ta'jiz means rendering powerless; man' means preventing.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Thus, the initial claim leads to an absurdity. The opponent's position is untenable.
This sets up the need for a proper understanding of divine power and human action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدور نفسه والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال.
فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه.
قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلاً عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة بالمتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار وعن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة، وفيما زعموا هو قادر على تحصيل مقدوره لو لم يمنعه غيره عن ذلك أو لم يعجزه، ويمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره بمنع العبد إياه لا باختياره، وهذا هو أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا.
Due to the opposition between motion and rest, and this is not disputed by any rational person. If this is so, then the establishment of God's power over His object of power becomes dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. If he did not refrain from acquiring his object of power, God's power over His object of power would not be established. Thus, God's power over His object of power was dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. The servant, in refraining from acquiring his object of power, is free (mukhtār): if he wills, he refrains; if he wills, he does not refrain. So he becomes free in removing God's power: if he wills, he removes it from His object of power; if he wills, he does not remove it. Removing power is disabling (taʿjīz) according to us, and according to you it is prevention (manʿ) due to the permissibility of joining power with prevention according to you. Both matters—prevention and disabling—are impossible (muḥāl).
If they say: We charge you with this: that the Exalted and High Creator would not be powerful over opposites, because if He were powerful over both, then if He brought one of the opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and a preventer of Himself from bringing about what is opposite, due to the impossibility of two opposites subsisting in one locus. And just as it is not permissible that the Exalted Creator be prevented or disabled by another, it is not permissible that He be prevented or disabled by Himself.
It is said: Indeed, God is powerful, according to us, over each one of the two opposites alternatively (ʿalā al-badal). Thus, He is described as being powerful to bring about rest in this locus in this state as a substitute for what He brought into it of motion, and similarly with inversion (qalb). He is not described as having power over the two opposites in absolute terms, because their conjunction is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power. By this, His power is not attached to His object of power by the choice of another. Rather, He is powerful to do whichever of the two opposites He wills, and whichever of the two opposites He creates, He creates by choice; and whichever of the two He refrains from, He refrains from by choice, not by prevention from Himself or from another. And that is a sign of the perfection of power. As for what they claim—that He is powerful to acquire His object of power if another does not prevent Him from that or disable Him—and He refrains from acquiring His object of power due to the servant's prevention of Him, not by His choice, this is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. Such disabling or prevention does not follow from affirming the servant's power of acquisition (kasb), because his acquisition is an object of God's power, and God is the one who brings it into existence. So in his engagement in acquisition, there is no removal of God's power from His object of power such that disabling or prevention would follow, unlike affirming the power of creation (takhalluq) as we have established.
Source pages p. 883

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. Al-Nasafi presents a rejection of the Ashʿarī claim that human free will would reduce God's power to a state of dependency. He begins by stating a premise: the opposition between motion and rest is undeniable. If God's power over an object depended on the servant's refraining from creating that object, then the servant would have the choice to remove God's power, which would imply disabling (taʿjīz) or prevention (manʿ)—both impossible. The objector then argues that this logic would also imply that God cannot be powerful over both opposites simultaneously (e.g., motion and rest in the same locus), because if He created one, He would prevent Himself from creating the other. Al-Nasafi's answer distinguishes that God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis (ʿalā al-badal): He has the power to create either one as He wills, but since simultaneous existence is impossible, it does not fall under power. Thus, God's power is not dependent on another's choice; His refraining from creating an opposite is by His own choice, not due to prevention. This shows perfection of power. Finally, Al-Nasafi contrasts this with the case of human acquisition (kasb): the servant's act is itself God's creation, so no removal of God's power occurs. The reasoning follows the author's own argumentative order, clarifying the Ashʿarī position on divine power and human acquisition.

التعجيز
المنع

Misconception: Human free will can curtail God's power over an object.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that if that were the case, God's power would be subject to human choice, which is impossible; God's power is independent.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what two impossible consequences follow if God's power depends on the servant refraining from acquiring his own object of power?
A) Disabling (ta'jiz) and prevention (man')
B) Creation (takwin) and annihilation (ifna')
C) Power and weakness
D) Acquisition (kasb) and creation (takhalluq)

Key Takeaway
God's power cannot be dependent on human choice; such dependency would be impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever live as though your choices can limit God's ability to act in your life? When has this pattern shown up recently? What would it mean to truly believe that God's power is never contingent on your refraining?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that making God's power dependent on human choice is impossible. Yet how often do we act as if God's response to our prayers depends on our worthiness or actions? How can you internalize that God's power is independent and absolute?
?
If you truly believed that nothing you do can add to or subtract from God's power, how would your daily reliance on Him change? What specific habit could you change today to reflect this truth?

God's Power over Opposites: Substitution and Human Acquisition
Al-Nasafi explains divine power over opposites on substitution and defends human acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's response that God's power over opposites is on substitution (badal) and why human acquisition does not remove God's power.

Core Idea
God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis, and human acquisition does not negate God's power.

Having established that human choice cannot remove God's power, al-Nasafi now addresses a counter-objection: if God is powerful over both motion and rest, then creating one would prevent Him from creating the other, implying limitation. He responds by clarifying that God's power is over each alternative on substitution. Moreover, he explains that human acquisition (kasb) does not involve removal of God's power because the acquisition itself is God's creation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The opponent argues: if God is powerful over both opposites, then creating one would mean He prevents Himself from creating the other, implying a limitation.
2
Learn the answer: substitution (badal)
Al-Nasafi explains that God is powerful over each opposite on a substitution basis: He can create either one as a substitute for the other. He is not described as powerful over both simultaneously.
This preserves God's power without implying contradiction.
3
Distinguish between impossibility and limitation
The simultaneous existence of opposites is impossible (muhal), and the impossible does not fall under power. Therefore, not being able to do the impossible is not a limitation.
4
Apply to human acquisition
Al-Nasafi then argues that in the case of human acquisition (kasb), the acquisition is itself created by God. Thus, when the servant acquires, God is not prevented from creating; rather, God creates the acquisition. So no removal of God's power occurs.
This is contrasted with the rejected view of creation (takhalluq) where the human creates independently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدور نفسه والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال.
فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه.
قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلاً عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة بالمتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار وعن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة، وفيما زعموا هو قادر على تحصيل مقدوره لو لم يمنعه غيره عن ذلك أو لم يعجزه، ويمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره بمنع العبد إياه لا باختياره، وهذا هو أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا.
Due to the opposition between motion and rest, and this is not disputed by any rational person. If this is so, then the establishment of God's power over His object of power becomes dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. If he did not refrain from acquiring his object of power, God's power over His object of power would not be established. Thus, God's power over His object of power was dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. The servant, in refraining from acquiring his object of power, is free (mukhtār): if he wills, he refrains; if he wills, he does not refrain. So he becomes free in removing God's power: if he wills, he removes it from His object of power; if he wills, he does not remove it. Removing power is disabling (taʿjīz) according to us, and according to you it is prevention (manʿ) due to the permissibility of joining power with prevention according to you. Both matters—prevention and disabling—are impossible (muḥāl).
If they say: We charge you with this: that the Exalted and High Creator would not be powerful over opposites, because if He were powerful over both, then if He brought one of the opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and a preventer of Himself from bringing about what is opposite, due to the impossibility of two opposites subsisting in one locus. And just as it is not permissible that the Exalted Creator be prevented or disabled by another, it is not permissible that He be prevented or disabled by Himself.
It is said: Indeed, God is powerful, according to us, over each one of the two opposites alternatively (ʿalā al-badal). Thus, He is described as being powerful to bring about rest in this locus in this state as a substitute for what He brought into it of motion, and similarly with inversion (qalb). He is not described as having power over the two opposites in absolute terms, because their conjunction is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power. By this, His power is not attached to His object of power by the choice of another. Rather, He is powerful to do whichever of the two opposites He wills, and whichever of the two opposites He creates, He creates by choice; and whichever of the two He refrains from, He refrains from by choice, not by prevention from Himself or from another. And that is a sign of the perfection of power. As for what they claim—that He is powerful to acquire His object of power if another does not prevent Him from that or disable Him—and He refrains from acquiring His object of power due to the servant's prevention of Him, not by His choice, this is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. Such disabling or prevention does not follow from affirming the servant's power of acquisition (kasb), because his acquisition is an object of God's power, and God is the one who brings it into existence. So in his engagement in acquisition, there is no removal of God's power from His object of power such that disabling or prevention would follow, unlike affirming the power of creation (takhalluq) as we have established.

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. Al-Nasafi presents a rejection of the Ashʿarī claim that human free will would reduce God's power to a state of dependency. He begins by stating a premise: the opposition between motion and rest is undeniable. If God's power over an object depended on the servant's refraining from creating that object, then the servant would have the choice to remove God's power, which would imply disabling (taʿjīz) or prevention (manʿ)—both impossible. The objector then argues that this logic would also imply that God cannot be powerful over both opposites simultaneously (e.g., motion and rest in the same locus), because if He created one, He would prevent Himself from creating the other. Al-Nasafi's answer distinguishes that God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis (ʿalā al-badal): He has the power to create either one as He wills, but since simultaneous existence is impossible, it does not fall under power. Thus, God's power is not dependent on another's choice; His refraining from creating an opposite is by His own choice, not due to prevention. This shows perfection of power. Finally, Al-Nasafi contrasts this with the case of human acquisition (kasb): the servant's act is itself God's creation, so no removal of God's power occurs. The reasoning follows the author's own argumentative order, clarifying the Ashʿarī position on divine power and human acquisition.

Divine Attributes

God Cannot Give Power Over What He Cannot Do
Nasafi presents a reductio ad absurdum and analogies to refute the possibility of God creating power for the incapable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is rationally impossible for God to create in a servant a power for an action that God Himself cannot perform.

Core Idea
You cannot give what you do not have.

The Mu'tazilites claimed that God can empower the servant to do actions that God Himself does not do. Imam Nasafi here refutes this by a series of logical arguments and analogies that appeal to common sense, showing the absurdity of such a position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's step-by-step reasoning.
This is a dense argument; take your time.
2
Understand the dilemma
The author presents a dilemma: either both God and the servant have independent power over the same act, or God's power is overridden. Both are impossible.
3
Consider the analogies
Nasafi uses analogies: a disabled person cannot empower another to walk, and a teacher cannot teach what they do not know. These illustrate the principle that one cannot give power over what one cannot do.
These analogies are meant to be intuitively obvious.
4
Appreciate the reductio
The author shows that the Mu'tazilite position leads to absurdities that even the common person would reject.
This strengthens the argument by appealing to universal reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة، وفيما زعموا هو قادر على تحصيل مقدوره لو لم يمنعه غيره عن ذلك أو لم يعجزه، ويمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره بمنع العبد إياه لا باختياره، وهذا هو أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا. والذي يؤيد ما ذكرنا أن كل فعل من أفعال العبد عرض وهو قبل حدوثه وخروجه من العدم إلى الوجود كان معلوم الباري جل وعلا بلا خوف، وهو عندهم جميعًا شيء، وعند البصريين منهم عوض، وعند الجبائي إن كان عند الوجد حركة فهو في حال العدم أيضا حركة، ثم لا شك أن في حال عدمه معلوم الله تعالى، والله تعالى يعلمه شيئا في حال عدمه، وعندهم وعند البصريين يعلمه عرضا وعند الجبائي منهم يعلمه حركة. ثم الحال لا يخلو إما إن كانت لله تعالى عليه قدرة كما للعبد عليه قدرة ويصح من كل واحد منهما الانفراد بإيجاده كما هو مذهب طائفة منهم، وإما إن كانت قدرة الله تعالى غير متيقنة لما كان مقدورًا للعبد لاستحالة كون مقدور لقادرين كما هو مذهب جمهورهم، ولا وجه إلى هذا؛ لأن الله تعالى هو الذي يتولى إعطاء العبد قدرة الفعل وهو المقدر له، ومن المحال أن يقدر ذات ما غيره على ما لا قدرة للمقدر عليه، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يقدر المقعد غيره على عين المشي الذي المقعد عنه عاجز وهو محال، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم. فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الباري جل جلاله إرادة الفعل لا يكون هذا مريدًا له، فلم لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه؟ قيل: عندنا لا فرق بين هذا وبين ما ألزمنا، فإن الله تعالى كما يستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لغيره على فعل لا قدرة له على ذلك الفعل يستحيل أن يخلق إرادة لغيره لفعل لا يكون هو مريدًا لذلك الفعل لما نبين بعد هذا أن من مذهبنا القول بعموم إرادة الله تعالى المحدثات، وهذا السؤال بنيتم على أصلكم الفاسد. فإن قالوا: القول بما قلتم يؤدي إلى أن يوجد من الله تعالى إرادة للمتضادين في محل واحد في وقت واحد، فإنه إذا خلق لذات ما إرادة لفعل في محل، وخلق لآخر إرادة ضد ذلك الفعل في عين ذلك المحل في تلك الساعة، وكان هو تعالى
Choice is not prevented by itself or by another, and it is a sign of perfection of power. According to their claim, he is able to acquire his possible object if no other prevents him from it or disables him, and he refrains from acquiring his possible object due to the servant's prevention not by his choice. This is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. Such disabling or prevention does not necessitate [God's incapacity] by establishing the servant's power over acquisition, because his acquisition is possible to God Almighty, and God Almighty is the one who brings it into existence. So in his engagement in acquisition there is no removal of God's power from His possible object to necessitate disabling or prevention, unlike the establishment of creative power as we have established. What supports what we have mentioned is that every action of the servant is an accident, and before its occurrence and its emergence from non-existence to existence, it was known to God Almighty without doubt. According to them all, it is a 'thing'; according to the Basrans among them, it is an 'accident'; according to al-Jubba'i, if it is a movement when found, then in the state of non-existence it is also a movement. Then there is no doubt that in its state of non-existence it is known to God Almighty, and God Almighty knows it as a thing in its state of non-existence. According to them and the Basrans, He knows it as an accident; according to al-Jubba'i among them, He knows it as a movement. Then the situation is not free from either: either God has power over it as the servant has power over it, and it is valid for each of them to independently bring it into existence, as is the doctrine of a group among them; or God's power is not certain [to be effective] when it is possible for the servant, due to the impossibility of a possible object being for two able agents, as is the doctrine of the majority of them. There is no way to this [latter position] because God Almighty is the one who undertakes to give the servant the power of action, and He is the one who empowers him. It is impossible for a being to empower another over what the empowerer has no power over. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for a disabled person to empower another to perform the very walking of which the disabled person is incapable, and that is impossible. Likewise, it is impossible for a being to teach another something that was not known to that teacher, without distinction between the eternal and the temporal. So this is similar. The impossibility of this is known by the common people with their innate intuitions and primary intellects. So much so that if the statement of the Mu'tazilites were presented to the dullest of God's creatures among the common people — their permitting God to create power for the servant over what God Himself cannot do, or for one of the servants to empower a being over what that being cannot do — they would hasten to consider the speaker foolish and to reject that as a doctrine. Just as they recognize the impossibility of a being teaching another what the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to consider foolish the one who permits that. That is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and primary intellects. So this is similar. Do you not see that the statement about creating power by one who is not capable of it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge by one who is not knowledgeable of it is impossible? Likewise, the statement about creating power for an action by one who is not capable of that action is impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known object by one who is not knowledgeable of that known object. If they say: Since it is permissible for God Almighty to create the intention for an action without His being the one intending it, why is it not permissible for Him to create power for an action without His having power over it? It is said: According to us, there is no difference between this and what we have imposed upon you. For just as it is impossible for God to create power for another over an action over which He has no power, it is impossible for Him to create intention for another for an action of which He is not the intender. As we will explain later, one of our doctrines is the affirmation of the universality of God's will for all temporal events. This question is built upon your corrupt principle. If they say: The statement you have made leads to the existence of two contradictory intentions from God in one locus at one time. For if He creates for a being an intention for an action in a locus, and He creates for another an intention for the opposite action in that same locus at that same moment, and He is —
Source pages p. 884

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that God can create in the servant a capacity to do actions that God Himself cannot do. The author begins by stating that the choice of the servant is not prevented by anything external, and that the servant's power is a sign of incapacity, not perfection. Then he argues that every action of the servant is an accident, known to God before it exists, and the Mu'tazilites disagree on its nature during non-existence. Then he presents a dilemma: either both God and the servant have independent power over the same act (as some Mu'tazilites claim) or God's power is overridden, which is impossible. He then demonstrates the absurdity by analogy: just as it is impossible to give knowledge of something unknown, it is impossible to give power over something one cannot do. The first objection tries to differentiate between creating intention and creating power, but the author denies the distinction because in both cases God must will the action. The second objection argues that this leads to contradictory wills in God, but the answer is cut off.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can give power over any action, even those He cannot do.
Correction: You cannot give what you do not have; God's power is consistent with His own capability.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why is it impossible for God to create power for a servant to do an action that God cannot do?
A) Because God cannot create anything.
B) Because power is like knowledge: one cannot give power over what one cannot do, just as one cannot teach what one does not know.
C) Because the servant is more powerful than God.
D) Because the action is an accident and cannot be created.

Key Takeaway
It is rationally impossible for God to create power over an action He cannot perform, as this would contradict the principle that one cannot give what one does not have.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God cannot give power over what He cannot do. Do you ever expect God to act against His own nature—for example, by granting a miracle that violates His established laws without purpose? Where in your life do you need to align your expectations with who God truly is, rather than what you wish He would do?
?
The analogy of the disabled person shows the absurdity of giving to others what you lack. Consider your own reliance on God: Are there areas where you try to rely on yourself or others to provide what only God can give? What would change if you fully admitted your own powerlessness before Him?
?
The passage says even the dullest person would reject the Mu'tazilite claim. When have you accepted a belief about God or about life that, upon honest reflection, does not hold up to simple reason? What comfort might you need to let go of to embrace the truth?

Objection and Answer on Intentions and Powers
Nasafi answers an objection about intentions and begins to address a second objection about contradictory wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objection regarding intentions and power, and Imam Nasafi's response that God's will is universal.

Core Idea
If God can create intentions He doesn't intend, He can create powers He doesn't have.

After presenting the main argument, Nasafi anticipates an objection: if God can create an intention for a servant without intending it, why can't He create power for a servant without having that power? Nasafi responds that God's will is universal, so creating intention implies He intends it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The Mu'tazilites argue that if God can create intention without intending, then He can create power without having power.
2
Understand Nasafi's answer
Nasafi denies the distinction: just as God cannot create power over what He cannot do, He cannot create intention for what He does not will.
He grounds this in the doctrine of universal will.
3
Note the second objection
The Mu'tazilites then object that this leads to contradictory wills in God. The passage ends mid-sentence.
The answer is incomplete due to the page break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة، وفيما زعموا هو قادر على تحصيل مقدوره لو لم يمنعه غيره عن ذلك أو لم يعجزه، ويمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره بمنع العبد إياه لا باختياره، وهذا هو أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا. والذي يؤيد ما ذكرنا أن كل فعل من أفعال العبد عرض وهو قبل حدوثه وخروجه من العدم إلى الوجود كان معلوم الباري جل وعلا بلا خوف، وهو عندهم جميعًا شيء، وعند البصريين منهم عوض، وعند الجبائي إن كان عند الوجد حركة فهو في حال العدم أيضا حركة، ثم لا شك أن في حال عدمه معلوم الله تعالى، والله تعالى يعلمه شيئا في حال عدمه، وعندهم وعند البصريين يعلمه عرضا وعند الجبائي منهم يعلمه حركة. ثم الحال لا يخلو إما إن كانت لله تعالى عليه قدرة كما للعبد عليه قدرة ويصح من كل واحد منهما الانفراد بإيجاده كما هو مذهب طائفة منهم، وإما إن كانت قدرة الله تعالى غير متيقنة لما كان مقدورًا للعبد لاستحالة كون مقدور لقادرين كما هو مذهب جمهورهم، ولا وجه إلى هذا؛ لأن الله تعالى هو الذي يتولى إعطاء العبد قدرة الفعل وهو المقدر له، ومن المحال أن يقدر ذات ما غيره على ما لا قدرة للمقدر عليه، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يقدر المقعد غيره على عين المشي الذي المقعد عنه عاجز وهو محال، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم. فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الباري جل جلاله إرادة الفعل لا يكون هذا مريدًا له، فلم لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه؟ قيل: عندنا لا فرق بين هذا وبين ما ألزمنا، فإن الله تعالى كما يستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لغيره على فعل لا قدرة له على ذلك الفعل يستحيل أن يخلق إرادة لغيره لفعل لا يكون هو مريدًا لذلك الفعل لما نبين بعد هذا أن من مذهبنا القول بعموم إرادة الله تعالى المحدثات، وهذا السؤال بنيتم على أصلكم الفاسد. فإن قالوا: القول بما قلتم يؤدي إلى أن يوجد من الله تعالى إرادة للمتضادين في محل واحد في وقت واحد، فإنه إذا خلق لذات ما إرادة لفعل في محل، وخلق لآخر إرادة ضد ذلك الفعل في عين ذلك المحل في تلك الساعة، وكان هو تعالى
Choice is not prevented by itself or by another, and it is a sign of perfection of power. According to their claim, he is able to acquire his possible object if no other prevents him from it or disables him, and he refrains from acquiring his possible object due to the servant's prevention not by his choice. This is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. Such disabling or prevention does not necessitate [God's incapacity] by establishing the servant's power over acquisition, because his acquisition is possible to God Almighty, and God Almighty is the one who brings it into existence. So in his engagement in acquisition there is no removal of God's power from His possible object to necessitate disabling or prevention, unlike the establishment of creative power as we have established. What supports what we have mentioned is that every action of the servant is an accident, and before its occurrence and its emergence from non-existence to existence, it was known to God Almighty without doubt. According to them all, it is a 'thing'; according to the Basrans among them, it is an 'accident'; according to al-Jubba'i, if it is a movement when found, then in the state of non-existence it is also a movement. Then there is no doubt that in its state of non-existence it is known to God Almighty, and God Almighty knows it as a thing in its state of non-existence. According to them and the Basrans, He knows it as an accident; according to al-Jubba'i among them, He knows it as a movement. Then the situation is not free from either: either God has power over it as the servant has power over it, and it is valid for each of them to independently bring it into existence, as is the doctrine of a group among them; or God's power is not certain [to be effective] when it is possible for the servant, due to the impossibility of a possible object being for two able agents, as is the doctrine of the majority of them. There is no way to this [latter position] because God Almighty is the one who undertakes to give the servant the power of action, and He is the one who empowers him. It is impossible for a being to empower another over what the empowerer has no power over. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for a disabled person to empower another to perform the very walking of which the disabled person is incapable, and that is impossible. Likewise, it is impossible for a being to teach another something that was not known to that teacher, without distinction between the eternal and the temporal. So this is similar. The impossibility of this is known by the common people with their innate intuitions and primary intellects. So much so that if the statement of the Mu'tazilites were presented to the dullest of God's creatures among the common people — their permitting God to create power for the servant over what God Himself cannot do, or for one of the servants to empower a being over what that being cannot do — they would hasten to consider the speaker foolish and to reject that as a doctrine. Just as they recognize the impossibility of a being teaching another what the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to consider foolish the one who permits that. That is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and primary intellects. So this is similar. Do you not see that the statement about creating power by one who is not capable of it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge by one who is not knowledgeable of it is impossible? Likewise, the statement about creating power for an action by one who is not capable of that action is impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known object by one who is not knowledgeable of that known object. If they say: Since it is permissible for God Almighty to create the intention for an action without His being the one intending it, why is it not permissible for Him to create power for an action without His having power over it? It is said: According to us, there is no difference between this and what we have imposed upon you. For just as it is impossible for God to create power for another over an action over which He has no power, it is impossible for Him to create intention for another for an action of which He is not the intender. As we will explain later, one of our doctrines is the affirmation of the universality of God's will for all temporal events. This question is built upon your corrupt principle. If they say: The statement you have made leads to the existence of two contradictory intentions from God in one locus at one time. For if He creates for a being an intention for an action in a locus, and He creates for another an intention for the opposite action in that same locus at that same moment, and He is —
Source pages p. 884

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that God can create in the servant a capacity to do actions that God Himself cannot do. The author begins by stating that the choice of the servant is not prevented by anything external, and that the servant's power is a sign of incapacity, not perfection. Then he argues that every action of the servant is an accident, known to God before it exists, and the Mu'tazilites disagree on its nature during non-existence. Then he presents a dilemma: either both God and the servant have independent power over the same act (as some Mu'tazilites claim) or God's power is overridden, which is impossible. He then demonstrates the absurdity by analogy: just as it is impossible to give knowledge of something unknown, it is impossible to give power over something one cannot do. The first objection tries to differentiate between creating intention and creating power, but the author denies the distinction because in both cases God must will the action. The second objection argues that this leads to contradictory wills in God, but the answer is cut off.

Key Terms
إرادة
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi respond to the Mu'tazilite objection that God can create intention without intending?
A) He admits it is possible.
B) He says there is no difference between intention and power; both are impossible for God to create if He does not will them.
C) He ignores the objection.
D) He says the objection is based on a corrupt principle, but gives no further explanation.

Key Takeaway
God's will is universal, so creating intention for an action implies He intends it, making the Mu'tazilite analogy invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that if God can create intentions without intending, then He can create powers without having power. Nasafi responded that both are impossible because God's will is universal over all temporal events. How often do you act as if God's will is not enough for the situations you face? What would change in your life if you truly believed that every intention and power comes from Him alone?
?
Read carefully: 'one of our doctrines is the affirmation of the universality of God's will for all temporal events.' What specific temporal event in your life right now are you reluctant to attribute to God's will? Are you willing to surrender that event to Him, even if it means accepting that His will is beyond your understanding?
?
The second objection suggests that Nasafi's position leads to contradictory intentions from God. How does this possibility challenge your need for God's actions to be logically consistent by human standards? Will you trust God's absolute sovereignty even when it appears contradictory to your finite mind? What is one area where you resist this trust?

Why God Cannot Create Power for an Impossible Act
Imam al-Nasafi proves by analogy that God cannot create power for an act He cannot do.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that it is impossible for God to create power in a creature for an action that God Himself cannot perform, based on the analogy with knowledge.

Core Idea
The creator must possess the attribute He creates; otherwise it's a contradiction.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful analogy to refute the Mu'tazilite position that God can create power in humans for actions God cannot do. He argues that just as it is impossible for God to create knowledge of something He does not know, so too it is impossible for Him to create power over something He is not powerful over. This argument appeals to both logical reasoning and innate human intuition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and analogy come through.
2
Identify the analogy used
The passage compares power to knowledge. Find how the author draws the parallel and what conclusion follows.
3
Note the appeal to common sense
The author says even common people would reject the Mu'tazilite view. Think about why this appeal strengthens the argument.
Innate intuition (badaha) is considered a reliable source of knowledge in kalam.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The key principle is that the creator must possess the attribute He creates. Reflect on why this is logically necessary.
Otherwise, the creation would involve a contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنه عاجز وهو محال ، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم.
It is impossible for Him, and likewise it is impossible that He should know something of another which is not known to this knowledge without distinction between the eternal and the originated. So likewise this. And the impossibility of this is something that the common people know by their innate intuitions and first principles of their intellects, so much so that if the statement of the Mu'tazila were presented to the most obtuse of God's creatures among the common people — concerning their allowing God to create power for the servant over what God Almighty is not powerful over Himself, or that any of the servants could empower a being over what that being is not powerful over — they would hasten to consider foolish the one who says it and is satisfied with that as his doctrine, just as they know the impossibility of teaching a being something that the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to consider foolish the one who permits that. And that is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and first principles of intellects. So likewise this. Do you not see that the statement about creating power from one who is not powerful over it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge from one who is not knowing of it is impossible? So likewise the statement about creating power for an act from one who is not powerful over that act would be impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known thing from one who is not knowing of that known thing.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage is a proof by analogy demonstrating that it is impossible for God to create power in a creature for an action that God Himself is not capable of performing. The author begins by stating that it is impossible for God to be incapable of something, and then draws an analogy with knowledge: just as it is impossible for God to create knowledge of something He does not know, so too it is impossible for Him to create power over something He is not powerful over. He emphasizes that this is intuitive even for common people, so much so that if the Mu'tazilite position were presented to them, they would immediately reject it as foolish. The argument relies on the principle that the creator must possess the attribute He creates, otherwise it would be a logical contradiction.

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
عاجز (incapable)
محال (impossible)
بداهة (innate intuition)
تخليق (creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can create power in a creature to do something God cannot do.
Correction: This is impossible because the creator must possess the attribute He creates. If God cannot do an act, He cannot create power for that act.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to prove that God cannot create power for an act He cannot do?
A) The analogy of knowledge: just as God cannot create knowledge of something He does not know.
B) The analogy of will: just as God cannot create will for something He does not will.
C) The analogy of life: just as God cannot create life for something He does not have.
D) The analogy of speech: just as God cannot create speech for something He does not say.

Key Takeaway
God cannot create power for an act He cannot do, just as He cannot create knowledge of something He does not know, because the creator must possess the attribute He creates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's power, do you ever imagine it as something He could 'lend out' or delegate, like a borrowed tool? How does this lesson's insistence that the Creator must possess every attribute He creates challenge that mental picture?
?
If even the most ignorant person recognizes the absurdity of God creating power for an act He cannot do, what does that say about your own intellectual pride when you are tempted to rationalize a view that contradicts clear reason?
?
This lesson uses an analogy between knowledge and power. In your own life, are there areas where you claim to 'know' something but do not 'act' on it? How does the inseparable connection between knowledge and action in God's attributes call you to align your own knowledge with practice?

Refuting the Objection: God Creates Will Without Being Willful
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite analogy by asserting the generality of God's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Maturidi doctrine, God cannot create will for an act without willing it, and why the Mu'tazilite analogy with power fails.

Core Idea
God's will is all-encompassing; He cannot create will for something He does not will.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi faces a clever objection from the Mu'tazila. They argue that if God can create will in a person without Himself being willing, He should similarly create power without being powerful. Nasafi's response hinges on the unique scope of God's will, which covers all created things. Let's examine the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage and its translation. Understand the analogy they propose: just as God creates will for an act without being willing, He should be able to create power without being powerful.
2
Examine Nasafi's refutation
Read the rest of the passage. Nasafi denies the analogy, stating that God's will is general over all created things, making it impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will.
The key difference between will and power is that God's will is all-encompassing, while power is not necessarily so in the same way.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Reflect on the Maturidi principle of 'عموم الإرادة' (generality of will). This doctrine means that God wills every created thing, so creating a will for a creature for an act implies that God wills that act as well.
This refutation shows that the Mu'tazilite objection is based on a misunderstanding of God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الباري جل جلاله إرادة الفعل لا يكون هذا مريدًا له، فلم لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه؟ قيل: عندنا لا فرق بين هذا وبين ما ألزمنا، فإن الله تعالى كما يستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لغيره على فعل لا قدرة له على ذلك الفعل يستحيل أن يخلق إرادة لغيره لفعل لا يكون هو مريدًا لذلك الفعل لما نبين بعد هذا أن من مذهبنا القول بعموم إرادة الله تعالى المحدثات، وهذا السؤال بنيتم على أصلكم الفاسد.
If they say: When it is permissible for the Exalted Creator to create will for an act without Him being willing of it, why is it not permissible for Him to create power over an act without being powerful over it? It is said: According to us, there is no difference between this and what we have imposed. For God, just as it is impossible for Him to create power for another over an act without being powerful over that act, it is impossible for Him to create will for another for an act without being willing of that act, because we will explain later that our doctrine holds the generality of God's will over originated things. And this question is based on your corrupt principle.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage presents a Mu'tazilite objection and the author's response. The objectors argue that since God can create will in a person for an action without Himself being willing of that action, He should also be able to create power in a person for an action without Himself being powerful over it. The author refutes by stating that according to his school (Maturidi doctrine), there is no such distinction: God's will is general over all created things, so it is impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will. The difference between will and power is that God's will is all-encompassing, so the analogy does not hold.

Key Terms
إرادة (will)
قدرة (power)
مريد (willing)
قادر (powerful)
عموم الإرادة (generality of will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that creating a will in a creature for an act does not require the creator to will that act, analogous to creating power.
Correction: According to Maturidi doctrine, God's will is all-encompassing (عموم الإرادة), so it is impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will. The analogy with power does not hold because will and power function differently with respect to God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can't God create will for an act without being willing of it?
A) Because God's will is general over all created things.
B) Because God cannot create anything.
C) Because will is not an attribute.
D) Because the Mu'tazila are wrong.

Key Takeaway
God's will is all-encompassing, so He cannot create a will for an act without willing it — a key Maturidi principle refuting the Mu'tazilite analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every desire you have is within God's will? Or do you sometimes feel you have independent will that God does not control? How does this lesson affect your view of your own intentions? Commit to repeating 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' daily to reaffirm that all will and power belong to Him.
?
If God's will encompasses all, then your good and bad intentions are created by Him. How does this make you feel about your responsibility? Does it lead you to rely more on Him or to despair? Today, ask God to purify your intentions and make you aware that even your turning to Him is by His will.
?
The Mu'tazilites denied the generality of God's will because they found it uncomfortable. Are there aspects of God's decree that you find hard to accept? Will you surrender to His will even when it conflicts with your own reasoning? Pray for the ability to accept His qadr fully.

Refuting the Claim that God's Will Can Embrace Contraries
Imam al-Nasafi answers the objection that creating wills for contrary acts would imply God wills impossible things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that God's creating wills for contrary acts leads to willing impossibilities is invalid, and how the distinction between will (irāda) and wish (tamannī) resolves it.

Core Idea
God's will is always effective; without an act, it is merely a wish.

Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key objection: if God creates wills for opposite actions in different people, wouldn't He be willing contradictory things? This would be impossible. The answer lies in a critical distinction: a will that does not result in the act is not truly will—it is a wish. Since God's will is always fulfilled, there is no contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objectors claim that if God creates wills for contrary acts in different loci at the same time, then God wills both contraries, which is impossible.
Note the structure of the objection: it assumes that any created will implies God's will for that act.
2
Find the answer's key move
The author immediately calls the objection deceptive or ignorant. Then he provides the core distinction: a will without a corresponding act is not a true will but a wish.
The decisive point: God only creates will for acts that actually occur.
3
Understand the implication
Since God is all-powerful, His will is always effective. So He cannot create a will for an act that does not happen. Thus, the scenario of two contrary created wills both being true wills cannot occur.
This refutes the objection without denying God's power.
4
Review the distinction between will and wish
The passage defines true will as accompanied by the act; otherwise it is wish. This is a key principle in Maturidi theology.
This distinction will be elaborated later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: القول بما قلتم يؤدي إلى أن يوجد من الله تعالى إرادة للمتضادين في محل واحد في وقت واحد، فإنه إذا خلق لذات ما إرادة لفعل في محل، وخلق لآخر إرادة ضد ذلك الفعل في عين ذلك المحل في تلك الساعة، وكان هو تعالى مريدًا ما خلق لكل واحد منهما إرادته من الفعل كان مؤديا إلى ذلك وهو محال. قيل: هذا السؤال تمويه منكم إن عرفتم حقيقة الإرادة وإلا فهو صادر عن الجهل بحقيقتها، وهذا لأن تخليق الإرادة لذاتين لفعلين متضادين في وقت واحد في محل واحد محال كتخليق فعلين، فإن الإرادة بدون الفعل محال وكل ما يظن إرادة إذا لم يطابقه الفعل ولم يقترن به فهو تمن وليس بإرادة فلا يكون كل واحد منهما إرادة بل ما قارنه الفعل فهو إرادة لم يقارنه الفعل فهو تَمَنِّ على ما نبين حقيقة هذا إذا انتهينا إلى مسألة الإرادة إن شاء الله تعالى.
If they say: The statement you have made leads to the existence from God of will for two contraries in one locus at one time. For if He creates for a being a will for an act in a locus, and creates for another a will for the contrary of that act in the same locus at that moment, and He is willing of what He created for each of them of will for the act, then that would lead to that, which is impossible. It is said: This question is a deception from you if you know the reality of will; otherwise it arises from ignorance of its reality. This is because the creation of will for two beings for two contrary acts at one time in one locus is impossible, like the creation of two acts. For will without an act is impossible. And everything that is thought to be will if the act does not correspond to it and is not accompanied by it, then it is a wish (tamannī) and not a will. So each of them is not a will, but rather that which the act accompanies is will; that which the act does not accompany is a wish, as we will explain the reality of this when we reach the question of will, God willing.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that the previous position (that God creates will in a creature only if He wills the corresponding act) would lead to God willing contraries simultaneously if He creates wills for contrary acts in different people. The author responds by distinguishing between true will (irāda) and wish (tamannī). True will must be accompanied by the act; if the act does not occur, it is merely a wish. Since God is all-powerful, His will always results in the act, so He cannot create a will for an act that does not occur. Therefore, there is no contradiction because God wills each act individually, and the creation of a will for a contrary act does not imply He wills it if the act does not follow.

Key Terms
إرادة
تمني
فعل
محل
متضادين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God could will two logically contradictory things at the same time because He is omnipotent.
Correction: God's will is always effective; thus He cannot will an act that does not occur. The scenario of contrary wills cannot arise because one of them would not be a true will.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a true will from a mere wish according to the author?
A) The occurrence of the act.
B) The strength of the desire.
C) The locus of the will.
D) The intention of the person.

Key Takeaway
God's will is always accompanied by its act; a will without an act is merely a wish, removing any contradiction of omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have a sincere intention to do a good deed that you have not yet acted upon? What does this lesson reveal about the true nature of that intention? Will you let it remain a mere wish, or will you accompany it with action?
?
If you find yourself repeatedly wishing to change a bad habit without ever making a concrete change, what does the distinction between will and wish say about the state of your heart? How can you take one small step today to turn that wish into a true will?
?
When you stand before Allah with your intentions, will they be accompanied by deeds, or will they be empty wishes that expose a lack of sincerity? What specific action can you commit to this week to ensure your will is true?
