Creative Power Belongs to God Alone; The Servant's Act Without Creation
Conclusion of argument against attributing creative power to anyone other than God, with a proof for the servant's act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming creative power for anyone other than God is tantamount to kufr and leads to absurdity, while the servant's act is affirmed without creative power.

Core Idea
Affirming creative power for other than God leads to shirk; the servant acts but does not create.

In this concluding passage, Imam Nasafi drives home the devastating consequence of the Mu'tazilite doctrine that humans can create like God. He argues that such a claim contradicts the Quran, makes its proponents deserving of worship, and implies justifying polytheism. He then reaffirms the orthodox position: the servant genuinely has an act, but that act is not creative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Pay attention to the author's strong language (kufr, absurdity).
2
Understand the Quranic argument
Identify the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ra'd 13:16) and how the author uses it to argue against the Mu'tazilite position.
The verse implies that if anyone else could create like God, it would justify worshipping them.
3
Grasp the servant's act without creation
Notice that the author affirms the servant has an act (fi'l) but not creative power. See how he uses the opponents' own agreement to support this.
This is a key distinction in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحقق ما رمنا (۱) تحقيقه من إثبات المشابهة بين خلق الله تعالى وخلق العباد على أصول المعتزلة، والله تعالى نفى ذلك فصاروا بذلك رادين على الله تعالى وجاعلين (۲) أنفسهم مستحقة للعبادة وأهلاً لها لأن الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ أَمْ (۳) جَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شركاء خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ، فَتَشَبَهَ الْخَلَقُ عَلَيْهِمْ (٤) أوجب لهم العذر في عبادتهم ما كانوا يعبدون وجعلهم إياهم شركاء الله تعالى في العبادة لو كان منهم خلق كخلقه، وكل ذلك كفر عصمنا الله تعالى عن مثل ذلك. وبالوقوف على ما بينا ظهرت صحة ما ادعينا أن إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى يؤدي إلى المحال، وبالله التوفيق. العبد له فعل وليست له قدرة التخليق]: ثم (٥) الدليل على أن العبد له فعل وإن لم تكن له قدرة التخليق مساعدة الخصوم إيانا أن له فعلاً، وما مر من الدلائل الموجبة لذلك وهي الدلائل
And what we intended to establish of the proof of similarity between the creation of God Almighty and the creation of the servants according to the principles of the Mu'tazila has been realized. God Almighty negated that, so they thereby become refuting God Almighty and making themselves deserving of worship and worthy of it, because God Almighty by His saying: 'Or have they attributed to God partners who created like His creation, so the creation seemed similar to them?' granted them an excuse in their worship of what they used to worship and made them partners of God Almighty in worship, if there had been from them a creation like His creation. All that is unbelief (kufr), may God protect us from the like of it. And by pausing upon what we have explained, the correctness of what we claimed appears: that affirming creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) for other than God Almighty leads to absurdity (al-muhāl). And with God is success. The servant has an act and he does not have creative power. Then the proof that the servant has an act even though he does not have creative power is the opponents' agreement with us that he has an act, and what has passed of the proofs necessitating that, and they are the proofs.
Source pages p. 899

Commentary
This passage serves as a conclusion to the preceding arguments and introduces a new proof. The author first states that he has successfully proven similarity between divine and human creation from the Mu'tazilite principles themselves. However, God has negated such similarity in the Quran (Surah al-Ra'd 13:16), and by claiming that they could create like God, the Mu'tazilites are effectively refuting God and making themselves deserving of worship. The Quranic verse grants polytheists an excuse for worshipping idols if those idols indeed created like God, but since they did not, the Mu'tazilite claim implies justifying shirk. The author declares this as kufr. He then summarizes that affirming creative power for other than God leads to absurdity (muhāl). After this conclusion, he begins a new section: 'The servant has an act and does not have creative power.' He presents the proof: the opponents themselves agree that the servant has an act, and there are additional proofs previously mentioned (which are not fully quoted here). The passage ends abruptly but conveys the main point: the servant's act is real, but it is not creative; creative power belongs solely to God.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق (qudrat al-takhlīq, creative power)
محال (muhāl, absurdity)
كفر (kufr, unbelief)
شركاء (shurakā', partners)
فعل (fi'l, act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the servant's act is entirely nonexistent or that humans have no real agency.
Correction: The author affirms that the servant has an act (fi'l), but denies that the servant has creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The act is real, but it is not a creative act in the divine sense.

Checkpoint
What consequence does the author say follows from affirming creative power for other than God?
A) It leads to the servant having no act at all.
B) It leads to absurdity and implies making partners with God in worship.
C) It leads to similarity between divine and human acts being impossible.
D) It leads to the rejection of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Affirming creative power for anyone other than God is kufr and leads to absurdity; the servant has an act but does not create.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something in your life—a success at work, a creative project, or even a good deed—do you ever feel a sense of pride that subtly attributes the outcome to your own independent power? How does this lesson expose that feeling as a potential form of shirk, and what will you do to shift your gratitude entirely to God?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought they were defending God's justice by affirming human creative power, yet the Quran calls their position kufr. Are there any beliefs or practices in your life that you think are righteous but actually contradict clear revelation? Will you have the courage to re-examine them in light of this lesson?
?
If the Quran grants polytheists an excuse for worshipping idols that truly create, how severe is the sin of attributing any creative power to yourself or others? Have you ever mentally 'partnered' anyone else with God in bringing about something good in your life? How can you repent from that and affirm that all creation is from Him alone?

Objection on God's Knowledge and Informing
Presents a shubha and the start of its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a key objection against the divine attribute of informing (iʿlām) and how it relates to God's knowledge.

Core Idea
God's information is not limited to the way He knows things.

This passage introduces a common objection: if God knows something in a specific way (e.g., as black), then He must inform us in exactly that way; otherwise, His information would be misleading. The text begins the refutation, setting the stage for a deeper discussion of how God's knowledge transcends human categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: it begins with 'شبهة والرد عليها' indicating an objection and a refutation.
2
Identify the condition
The objection states that if God knows something in a certain way, He must inform us on the same 'face' (wajh). Otherwise, it would be tajhīl (ignorance). Mark this conditional claim.
3
Notice the beginning of the answer
The phrase 'وهكذا الجواب' shows that the refutation has started. The text cuts off, but the implication is that the answer will challenge the assumption that God's knowledge and His information must be identical in mode.
The full answer is not present in this window, so we must be cautious not to speculate.

Source Text

For if He knows something as black or white or long or wide, and He informs us in that way, then [the text breaks off]

Commentary
This passage introduces a new objection (shubha) and begins the answer. The objection states: When God knows something in a certain way (e.g., as black or white), then if He informs us about it, He must inform us in accordance with His knowledge. If He informs us otherwise, that would not be true information but rather would be misleading (tajhīl). The text breaks off at 'بأن', presumably continuing the argument on a later page. The heading 'شبهة والرد عليها' indicates that a refutation follows, but only the beginning is present in this window. This lesson is incomplete but represents a distinct objection-answer unit.

Refuting the Objection by Analogy with Divine Knowledge
Refutation by analogy with divine knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that God cannot give us power over His creation by using a parallel between divine knowledge and divine power, and why the objection would imply impossibility in God.

Core Idea
If God cannot make us know what He doesn't know, He cannot give us power over what He doesn't do.

This passage tackles a critical objection: If God is the sole creator, how can humans have any real power? The author responds by comparing the relationship of divine and human knowledge to that of divine and human power. Just as both can know the same thing in different ways, both can have power over the same act in different respects. Understanding this analogy is key to the Maturidi doctrine of kasb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the argument structure: the author first states a premise, then draws an analogy, then refutes the objection by showing it leads to absurdity.
Pay attention to the repeated parallel structure: 'like this, so likewise that'.
2
Identify the key analogy
The author compares the impossibility of God making us know contrary to His knowledge with the impossibility of giving us power over contrary to His power. This is the central move of the refutation.
The analogy relies on the concept of 'attribution' (idafa) — everything known is attributed to God's knowledge, everything created is attributed to His power.
3
Understand the consequences of the objection
If the objection were true, it would imply that God could be rendered incapable (ta'jiz), which is impossible. Also, it would allow for creation not attributed to God, which would be like knowledge not attributed to Him — both false.
This shows the objection leads to theological absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محال بالإجماع، فتكون قدرة العبد متعلقة لا بجهة الاختراع ضرورة، فأما كون المعلوم معلومًا بعلمين فليس بمحال فيتعلق به علمه تعالى وعلمنا، والذي يؤيد ما قلنا: أن اعتبار العلم يوجب ما ذهبنا إليه أن إعلام الغير ممن لا علم له به محال، وإنما يصح إعلام الغير ممن له العلم، فكذا إقدار الغير على شيء لا قدرة للمقدور عليه يكون محالاً، وكذا زوال العلم عما هو معلوم غيره لا يكون إلا عن جهل، فكذا زوال القدرة عما هو مقدور الغير لن يكون إلا عن عجز، فكان فيما قلتم تعجيز الله تعالى وذلك محال.
ثم نقول لهم: لما كان يستحيل أن يعلمنا الله تعالى خلاف معلومه يستحيل أن يقدرنا الله تعالى على خلاف مقدوره، ومقدوره مخترع يضاف إليه لا مطلق المخترع، فبقدرنا أيضا على مخترع مضاف إليه لا على مطلق المخترع، ولو جاز أن يقدرنا على مخترع غير مضاف إليه لجاز أن يعلمنا معلومًا غير مضاف إليه وذا باطل، فكذا هذا.
It is impossible by consensus, so the power of the servant is attached only to the aspect of invention by necessity. As for something known being known by two knowledges, that is not impossible, so His knowledge and our knowledge attach to it. And what supports what we said: that consideration of knowledge necessitates what we have held: that informing another who has no knowledge of it is impossible, and informing another is only valid from one who has knowledge. Likewise, giving power to another over something over which the one giving power has no power is impossible. And likewise, the removal of knowledge from what is known by another only occurs through ignorance, so likewise the removal of power from what is the object of power of another will only be through incapacity. So in what you have said there is rendering God incapable, and that is impossible.
Then we say to them: Since it is impossible for God to make us know contrary to His knowledge, it is impossible for God to give us power over contrary to His object of power. And His object of power is an invention attributed to Him, not invention absolutely. So we also have power over an invention attributed to Him, not over invention absolutely. And if it were permissible for Him to give us power over an invention not attributed to Him, it would be permissible for Him to make us know something not attributed to Him, and that is false; so likewise this.
Source pages p. 904

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author begins by stating a premise that is agreed upon: it is impossible (by consensus) that a servant's power be related to the aspect of invention (ikhtira'). Then he draws an analogy: just as a thing can be known by both God's knowledge and our knowledge without contradiction, so too an act can be under both God's power and our power in different respects. He argues that if it were possible for God to give us power over something He Himself cannot do, it would imply incapacity in God, which is absurd. Similarly, if God could give us power over an invention not attributed to Him, then He could also give us knowledge of something not known by Him—both false. Thus the objection fails because it would lead to impossible consequences.

Key Terms
قدرة
اختراع
مقدور
معلوم
تعجيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the author denies any human power.
Correction: The author affirms human power over acquired acts, not over invention (creation ex nihilo).

Checkpoint
What does the author compare to the impossibility of God giving us power over His creation?
A) The impossibility of God giving us knowledge contrary to His knowledge
B) The impossibility of two agents acting on one object
C) The impossibility of God creating evil
D) The impossibility of human free will

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the objection by showing that if God could give us power over His creation, it would imply that God could be incapacitated or that creation could be independent of Him—both impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something you worked hard for, do you truly feel that your power is only over what God has already ordained? If not, what part of your heart still claims independent creation?
?
If God cannot be made incapable by your actions, why do you sometimes fear that your failures or sins have diminished His control? Where in your life do you need to trust His unshared power?
?
The author argues that giving power to you over what God alone creates would imply God's ignorance. Do you live as though God's knowledge and power are sufficient, or do you secretly doubt His sovereignty when life doesn't go your way?

Answering the Charges of Compulsion and Divine Powerlessness
The author answers the objection that his view entails compulsion or limiting God's power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi view of kasb avoids the twin charges of compulsion (jabr) and divine powerlessness (ta'jiz) by showing that the servant's intention is a genuine cause for God's creation.

Core Idea
The servant's intention is the condition for God's creation, not compulsion.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi tackles a common objection against the Maturidi theory of acquisition (kasb). Critics argue that if God creates all human acts, then either the servant can refuse (making God powerless) or cannot refuse (making the servant compelled). Nasafi responds by clarifying the relationship between divine creation and human intention, showing that voluntary acts are created precisely when the servant freely intends them.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage where the objection is presented. Note the two horns of the dilemma.
The objection assumes that if God creates the act, the servant must either have or lack the power to refuse.
2
Identify the two proofs the author relies on
Find where Nasafi says 'we have established by proof that there is no invention from the servant, and that he has an act.' Understand that these are the foundations of his answer.
These proofs show that the servant is neither the independent creator nor completely passive.
3
Examine the two cases of divine will
Read the last part where Nasafi distinguishes between necessary movements and voluntary movements. Notice how the servant's intention plays a role in the voluntary case.
For voluntary acts, the servant genuinely intends and chooses, and God creates the act in accordance with that intention.
4
Reflect on the resolution
Think about why the dilemma fails. The objection treats power of refusal as absolute, but Nasafi shows that refusal is impossible when the act is created concurrently with the servant's power.
The key is that the servant's power is simultaneous with the act's existence, so 'refusal' becomes meaningless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الوجه يبطل أيضًا قولهم إن ما قلتم يؤدي إلى جعل العباد مضطرين أو إلى تعجيز الله تعالى فإن الله تعالى إذا أراد أن يخلق كسب العبد إن كان للعبد قوة الامتناع فقد عجز الله تعالى عن تخليقه وإن لم يكن له قدرة الامتناع فهو إذًا مضطر
فإنا نقول: ثبتنا بالدليل أن لا اختراع من قبل العبد وأن له فعلاً كان مجموع الدليلين موجبًا كونه تعالى قادرًا مخترعًا، وكون العبد فاعلاً مكتسباً مختارا.
وما قلتم من السؤال يوجب بطلان أحد هذين الوجهين، وما ثبت بالدليل المتيقن غير محتمل للبطلان، فإذا كان السؤال في نفسه باطلاً.
ثم نقول: إن كان الله تعالى أراد الحركة الضرورية من العبد فيخلقه ولا يكون للعبد قدرة الامتناع والله تعالى قادر والعبد مضطر، وإن أراد تخليق الحركة الاختيارية فالعبد لا يتصور منه الامتناع لأنه تعالى إنما يخلق تلك الحركة إذا أرادها العبد واختار وقصد اكتسابها فيخلق الله تعالى لا محالة لإجرائه العادة في تخليقه عند وجود قصد العهد لا لكونه ملجأ إلى ذلك، على أن الله تعالى إذا كان يخلقه مقارنا لقدرة العبد كيف يتصور منه الامتناع عن الفعل وهو موجود والامتناع عن الموجود محال، والله الموفق.
And in this way their statement is also invalidated: that what you say leads to making servants compelled or to rendering God incapable, for if God wills to create the acquisition of the servant, if the servant has power of refusal, then God is incapable of creating it; and if he has no power of refusal, then he is compelled.
So we say: We have established by proof that there is no invention from the servant, and that he has an act. The sum of the two proofs necessitates that He, exalted, is powerful and inventing, and that the servant is a doer, acquirer, and chooser.
And what you mention of the question necessitates the invalidation of one of these two aspects, and what is established by certain proof is not liable to invalidation. So the question itself is invalid.
Then we say: If God, exalted, willed the necessary movement from the servant, He creates it, and the servant has no power of refusal, and God is powerful and the servant is compelled. And if He wills to create the voluntary movement, then refusal from the servant is inconceivable, because He only creates that movement when the servant wills it, chooses it, and intends to acquire it. So God creates it necessarily, due to His habit of creating upon the existence of the servant's intention, not because He is forced to that. Moreover, if God creates it concurrent with the servant's power, how can refusal of the act be conceived while it exists? And refusal of the existent is impossible. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 904

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection and provides an answer. The author first states the objection: if the Maturidi view holds that God creates all acts, then either the servant has the power to refuse (imtina')—making God unable to create the act—or the servant has no such power, making him compelled (mudtarr). The author responds by reaffirming the dual proofs: the servant has no power of invention (ikhtira') but has an act of kasb (acquisition). Thus, the dilemma is false. He explains that for voluntary acts, God creates them precisely when the servant intends and chooses them, so the servant is not compelled—his intention is a genuine cause for creation. The servant cannot refuse an act that is already being created by God concurrently with his power; refusal of an existent act is impossible. Therefore, the objection collapses.

Key Terms
مضطر
تعجيز
قوة الامتناع
كسب
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi view denies human choice and makes humans compelled in all actions.
Correction: The Maturidi view affirms that for voluntary acts, the servant genuinely intends and chooses the act, and God creates it in accordance with that intention. Thus, the servant is the acquirer (kāsib) of the act, not merely a passive recipient.

Checkpoint
What is the key point in the author's answer to the charge of compulsion?
A) The servant has no intention or choice
B) God creates voluntary acts only when the servant wills and intends them
C) The servant has power of invention like God
D) The objection is correct but we accept compulsion

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view of kasb shows that the servant's intention is a real cause for God's creation of the act, thus preserving human choice without attributing independent creation to the servant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look back at your worst sins, do you genuinely believe that you chose them and that your intention was real, or do you secretly feel that you were compelled by your desires? How can the lesson's distinction between necessary and voluntary movements help you own your choices before God?
?
The passage says that for voluntary movements, the servant cannot refuse because the act already exists. How does this truth challenge any excuse you make for continuing in a sin after committing it? Will you now accept full responsibility for your actions as a condition of repentance?
?
If God only creates your action when you intend it, what does that mean for the moments you claim 'I didn't mean to'? Will you examine your heart more honestly before God, knowing that your intention is the very cause of His creation of your deed?

One Act Under Two Powers
The author concludes that one act can be under two powers based on prior proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that a single act can be subject to two powers—God's creative power and the servant's acquired power—based on the distinction between creating and acquiring.

Core Idea
One act can be attributed to two agents: God creates, the human acquires.

This passage concludes a complex discussion in Maturidi kalam. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, has already argued that the servant cannot have the power to create (takhliq) but does have an acquired power (kasb). Here, he draws the logical conclusion: a single act can fall under two powers, each in a different respect. This is a key doctrine that distinguishes Maturidism from other theological schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's conclusion.
Pay attention to the phrase 'دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين جائز'.
2
Identify the two referenced proofs
The passage mentions two proofs: (1) the impossibility of the servant having the power of creation, and (2) the proof that the servant does have action and power (acquisition). Understand how these lead to the conclusion.
The author considers this combination sufficient and dispenses with further proofs.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'two powers'
Consider how one act can be attributed to both God and the servant without conflict. The Maturidi view distinguishes: God is the creator of the act, the servant is the acquirer (muktasib).
This avoids the extremes of Jabriyya (compulsion) and Qadariyya (total free will).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين جائز
وبالوقوف على ما بينا من دليل استحالة ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد، ودليل ثبوت الفعل والقدرة له يعرف جواز دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين بحمد الله تعالى دليل فيه كفاية وغنية عن الاشتغال بغيره من الدلائل.
وذلك ثم نقول: قد سبق منا القول في الفصل الذي أثبتنا فيه استحالة دخول الاختراع تحت قدرة العبد، وأن إقدار الغير على ما لا يقدر عليه المقدر محال
That one object of power falls under the power of two powerful agents is permissible.
And by standing upon what we have clarified of the proof of the impossibility of the power of creation being established for the servant, and the proof of the establishment of action and power for him, the permissibility of one object of power falling under the power of two powerful agents is known. Praise be to God, there is in it a sufficient proof and independence from occupying oneself with other proofs.
And then we say: Our discourse has already preceded in the chapter in which we established the impossibility of invention entering under the power of the servant, and that giving power to another over what the one giving power has no power over is impossible.
Source pages p. 905

Commentary
This is a concluding passage. The author declares the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) for one object of power (maqdur) to fall under the power of two agents. He refers back to two previously established proofs: (1) the impossibility of the servant having power of creation (takhliq), and (2) the proof that the servant does have an act and a power (in the sense of acquisition). By considering both proofs together, one understands that one act can be attributed to both God and the servant in different respects—God as Creator, the servant as acquirer (muktasib). He considers this sufficient and dispenses with further arguments. The final sentence reiterates that giving power to another over something the giver cannot do is impossible, thus the servant's power cannot be over creation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'one act under two powers' means both agents are equally creators.
Correction: The Maturidi view distinguishes: God creates the act, the human acquires it. Their powers are different in kind.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of one act being under two powers is a logical consequence of the distinction between divine creation and human acquisition.

The author says this proof is sufficient and you need not seek further. Have you accepted this with certainty, or is there doubt lingering? What concrete step will you take this week to deepen your conviction in divine creation and human accountability?

One Act Under Two Powers: Refuting the Mu'tazilite Objection
Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazilite denial of one act under two powers using consensus and distinction between invention and acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that a single act can be under two powers (divine and human) from different aspects, and how he refutes the Mu'tazilite denial.

Core Idea
One act can be under two powers from different aspects: invention and acquisition.

Al-Nasafi tackles a key theological dispute: can one act be attributed to both God and the human agent? The Mu'tazilites reject this, but al-Nasafi argues from consensus and logical necessity. In this passage, he clarifies the precise point of contention and exposes the flaw in the Mu'tazilite reasoning, which relies on imagination rather than rational analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the flow: consensus, evidence, distinction, refutation.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the consensus argument
Find where al-Nasafi states the consensus that God creates human power. Understand how this leads to the permissibility of one act under two powers.
This is the foundation of his argument.
3
Understand the distinction between invention and acquisition
Al-Nasafi clarifies that both sides agree it's impossible for two powers to attach from the same aspect (invention). The real dispute is about different aspects (invention and acquisition).
This distinction is crucial.
4
Critique of Mu'tazilite use of imagination
Note how al-Nasafi criticizes the Mu'tazilites for relying on imagination (wahm) instead of reason. This is a rhetorical and methodological point.
5
Review the conclusion
Al-Nasafi states that he has provided evidence for permissibility, let alone necessity. Reflect on why this matters for Ashʿarī theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد انعقد الإجماع أن الله تعالى هو الذي يقدر العبد ويخلق قدرته، وأن القدرة ليست بداخله تحت قدرة العبد إذ لو منعت منه لما تمكن من اكتسابها عندنا وتخليقها عندهم، وإذا كان الله تعالى هو الذي يقدر العبد كان محالاً أن يقدره على ما لاقدرة له عليه على ما قررنا، فكان ذلك دليلاً على جواز دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين، ثم لا دليل يدل للمعتزلة على استحالة دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين، إلا أنهم لم يعاينوا ذلك وهم أبدا يفزعون إلى الوهم ويجعلونه عيارا للعقل والفهم وهو بعيد عن الصواب على ما قررنا.
ثم قيل لهم أيش تعنون بقولكم إن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين محال ؟ أتعنون دخوله من جهة الاختراع أو من جهة الاكتساب أو من جهة اكتساب و اختراع؟ فإن قالوا من جهة الاختراع فسلم تنازعهم في هذا ، وإن قالوا: من جهة الاكتساب فكذلك لأن فعلاً واحدًا لا يكون فعلا لكاسبين. وإن قالوا من جهة الاكتساب والاختراع أن يقدر على اختراعه مخترع وعلى اكتسابه مكتسب ففيه النزاع.
فقيل لهم : لم قلتم ذلك وقد وقعت الخصومة فيه ثم ما أقمنا من الدلائل موجب ذلك ومن عد الممكن ممتنعا فهو جاهلي فكيف بمن عد الواجب ممتنعا؟
ثم هم إنما عدوا ذلك ممتنعا لأنهم لم يعقلوا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور إلا من جهة الاختراع وذلك لعمري ،محال وعند خصومهم قط لا يجوز تعلق قدرتين بجهة الاختراع بمقدور واحد وإنما الكلام وراء ذلك وهو أن قدرة واحدة لما تعلقت بمقدور بجهة الاختراع هل يجوز أن تتعلق به قدرة أخرى يكون أثرها جعل ذلك المخترع فعلا له أم لا؟ الجواز. عندنا ذلك جائز وعندهم ذلك ممتنع، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على فضلاً وجوبه
And consensus has been established that God Almighty is the one who empowers the servant and creates his power, and that power is not within the servant's control, for if it were withheld from him, he would not be able to acquire it according to us, nor would it be created according to them. And since God Almighty is the one who empowers the servant, it is impossible that He empower him over what he has no power over, as we have established. So that was evidence for the permissibility of a single act of power (maqdūr) falling under the power of two agents. Then there is no evidence for the Mu'tazilites of the impossibility of a single act of power falling under the power of two agents, except that they have not witnessed it, and they always resort to imagination (wahm) and make it the standard for reason and understanding, and that is far from correctness, as we have established. Then it was said to them: What do you mean by your statement that the entry of a single act of power under the power of two agents is impossible? Do you mean its entry from the aspect of invention (ikhtirāʿ) or from the aspect of acquisition (iktisāb) or from the aspect of acquisition and invention? If they say from the aspect of invention, then we concede the dispute concerning this. And if they say from the aspect of acquisition, likewise, because a single act cannot be an act for two acquirers. And if they say from the aspect of acquisition and invention, that an inventor (mukhtariʿ) can invent it and an acquirer (muktasib) can acquire it, then therein lies the dispute. So it was said to them: Why did you say that, when the contention has occurred about it, and we have presented proofs necessitating that? And whoever counts the possible as impossible is ignorant, so how about one who counts the necessary as impossible? Then they only counted that as impossible because they did not conceive the attachment of power to the act of power except from the aspect of invention, and that, by my life, is impossible. And according to their opponents, the attachment of two powers to a single act of power from the aspect of invention is not permissible at all. Rather, the discussion is beyond that: When a single power is attached to an act of power from the aspect of invention, is it permissible that another power be attached to it, whose effect is to make that invented thing an act for him? The answer: permissibility. According to us, that is permissible; according to them, it is impossible. And we have presented evidence for [its permissibility], let alone its necessity.
Source pages p. 906

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that one act of power (maqdūr) cannot fall under the power of two agents. Al-Nasafi begins by asserting a consensus (ijmāʿ) that God creates the servant's power, and the servant's power is not independent. If God gives the servant power, He cannot give power over what is impossible for the servant. This leads logically to the permissibility of one object being under two powers (God's and the servant's) from different aspects. He then criticizes the Mu'tazilites for relying on imagination (wahm) rather than reason. Next, he clarifies the point of contention by distinguishing between invention (ikhtirāʿ) and acquisition (iktisāb). The Mu'tazilites mistakenly assume that power attachment is only through invention, but the real issue is whether a power for acquisition can attach to the same object that God invented. Al-Nasafi confirms that this is possible; the Ashʿarī position affirms permissibility, while the Mu'tazilites deny it. He concludes by stating that they have provided proof for permissibility, let alone necessity.

Key Terms
الإجماع
القدرة
المقدور
الاختراع
الاكتساب
الوهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite objection is based on sound reason.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that the Mu'tazilites rely on imagination (wahm) rather than reason, and they misunderstand the different aspects of power attachment.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of contention al-Nasafi identifies between the Ashʿarīs and Muʿtazilites regarding one act of power?
A) Whether one act can be under two powers from the same aspect of invention.
B) Whether one act can be under two powers from different aspects (invention and acquisition).
C) Whether God creates human acts directly or indirectly.
D) Whether power can attach to an act from the aspect of acquisition.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi demonstrates that one act can be under two powers (divine and human) by distinguishing between invention and acquisition, and by appealing to consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept that every action you perform is both created by God and acquired by you? How does this balance affect your sense of responsibility for your sins? Today, will you consciously 'acquire' one good deed by intent, acknowledging God as its inventor?
?
When you fail, do you blame your circumstances or your own choice? How does al-Nasafi's distinction between invention and acquisition call you to own your failures? What is one area of your life where you need to stop excusing yourself and take responsibility?
?
The Mu'tazilites rejected the truth because they relied on their imagination rather than sound reasoning. In your life, are there truths about God's power that you resist because they don't fit your mental framework? Will you submit your imagination to revelation and reason from this lesson?

Refutation of the Objection that One Act Cannot Be by Two Agents
Refutes the claim that a single act cannot be attributed to two agents, defending the Maturidi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi and Ash'ari traditions refute the objection that a single act cannot be attributed to two agents, by distinguishing between the generic and specific names of acts and the role of acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
A single act can be attributed to God and servant in different respects—God as creator, servant as locus.

In this passage, the author defends the Maturidi position against a common objection: if one act could be by two agents, then one speech could be by two speakers. The response clarifies that 'act' is a general term with subcategories; what is God's act in one sense is the servant's act in another, preventing any logical absurdity. The author also shows how Ash'ari and other scholars agree, using the concept of acquisition (kasb).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection
Read the opening lines of the passage to understand the opponent's claim and why it seems problematic at first glance.
The opponent uses an analogy: if one act by two agents, then one speech by two speakers.
2
Follow the Maturidi response
Note how the author distinguishes between God's act (an eternal attribute) and the servant's act (God's object of action) and then introduces the distinction between generic and specific names.
This is the core of the Maturidi argument.
3
Examine the Ash'ari and other views
The author shows that the objection also fails for Ash'aris and others because they use the concept of acquisition (kasb), where the attribute subsists in the servant while God is the creator.
Pay attention to terms like 'khalq' and 'kasb'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى من اتباع الوساوس والوقوع في ترهات البسابس، ومما يصولون على خصومهم بقولهم : لوجاز أن يكون فعل واحد فعلاً لفاعلين جاز أن يكون قول واحد قولاً لقائلين . يبطل بهذا أيضًا على ما قررنا أن الحركة الواحدة عندهم فعل لفاعلين ولم ينفعهم التجاهل ثم نقول : إن هذا الكلام لا يتوجه علينا فإنا لا نقول إن فعلاً واحدًا يكون فعلاً لفاعلين البتة، فإن ما هو فعل الله تعالى هو صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته وليس بفعل للعبد وما هو فعل للعبد ليس بفعل الله تعالى بل هو مفعوله، ثم الفعل اسم عام وله أسماء وأنواع ، فإن كان ما خلقه الله تعالى من فعل العبد ضربًا فهو معقول الله تعالى وفعل العبد باعتبار اسم جنسه و ضربه باعتبار اسم نوعه، وكذا لو خلق قول العبد فهو مفعول الله تعالى وهو فعل العبد باعتبار اسم جنسه وقوله باعتبار اسم نوعه، وكذا على قول أبي عيسى البرغوث وأبي حسن الأشعري لا يتوجه الإلزام فإنهما لا يجعلان فعلاً واحد لفاعلين بل لا فعل إلا لله تعالى، فأما العبد فله الكسب وقول العبد اسم لكسبه فيكون قوله فعلاً الله تعالى كسبًا للعبد، ثم ما هو من الأسماء للكسب يكون راجعا إلى من قام به الكسب فإن كان ذلك ضربًا فالضارب من قام به لا من خلقه والمتحرك من قامت به الحركة لا من خلقها، و القائل من قام به القول لا من خلقه، ولا يتصور قيام شيء من هذه المعاني إلا بمحل واحد فلا يوصف به اثنان، فأما الاتصاف بكونه فاعلاً ليس من شرطه قيام الفعل بالفاعل عندهم، ويحتجون عليكم في ذلك بالحركة والصفات الضرورية، فإن الفاعل للحركة الضرورية خالقها والمتحرك بها محلها، ولا يتصور اتصاف ذاتين بأنهما متحركان بحركة واحدة لاستحالة قياسها بذاتين، وكذا هذا في السواد فإن فاعله هو الله تعالى والأسود به المحل القابل له، وكذا في غيره من الصفات، فعلاً وكذا لا يلزم النجار وعبد الله بن سعيد والقلانسي وغيرهم حيث يجوزون لفاعلين أحدهما خالق والآخر مكتسب لأنهم لا يشترطون قيام الخلق بالخالق، وأنتم ساعدتموهم ويشترطون قيام الفعل الذي هو كسب بالمكتسب، وأنتم أيضا ساعدتموهم في ذلك، والقول اسم للكسب الخاص كالحركة والسواد وغيرهما فيكون الموصوف به المحل لا غير فأما من حيث إن القول تتعلق به قدرة الخالق وقدرة المكتسب لا تفارق غيره من الأفعال غير أن الموصوف باسمه النوعي من قام به على ما قررنا. وبالوقوف على هذا التقرير ظهر أن هذا تمويه وتلبيس على الضعفاء، والله الموفق.
Exalted be He from following whisperings and falling into absurdities of evil omens. And among the things they attack their opponents with is their saying: If it were permissible for one act to be an act of two agents, then it would be permissible for one speech to be a speech of two speakers. This is also invalidated on the basis of what we established, that in their view one movement is an act of two agents, and their feigning ignorance does not benefit them. Then we say: This speech does not apply to us, for we do not say that a single act is an act of two agents at all. For what is the act of God, exalted is He, is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and it is not an act of the servant. And what is an act of the servant is not an act of God, exalted is He, but rather is His object of action. Then act (fi‘l) is a general noun, and it has names and types. So if what God, exalted is He, created from the servant's act is a hitting (ḍarb), then it is intelligible as God's and as the servant's act by consideration of its generic name, and his hitting by consideration of its specific name. Similarly, if He created the servant's speech, it is an object of God's action and it is the servant's act by consideration of its generic name, and his speech by consideration of its specific name. Similarly, according to the saying of Abu Isa al-Burghuth and Abu Hasan al-Ash'ari, the objection does not apply, for they do not make one act for two agents; rather there is no act except for God, exalted is He. As for the servant, he has acquisition (kasb), and the servant's speech is a name for his acquisition, so his speech is an act of God, exalted is He, and an acquisition for the servant. Then what is among the names for acquisition refers to the one in whom the acquisition subsists. So if that is hitting, then the hitter is the one in whom it subsists, not the one who created it. The mover is the one in whom the movement subsists, not the one who created it. The speaker is the one in whom the speech subsists, not the one who created it. And it is inconceivable for any of these meanings to subsist except in a single locus, so they are not described for two. As for being described as an agent (fā‘il), it is not a condition for it that the act subsist in the agent according to them. And they argue against you in that by movement and essential attributes. For the agent of the essential movement is its creator, and the one moved by it is its locus. And it is inconceivable for two essences to be described as being moved by one movement, due to the impossibility of it subsisting in two essences. Similarly is this regarding blackness, for its agent is God, exalted is He, and the black by it is the locus receptive to it. Similarly in other attributes, act. Similarly, it does not apply to al-Najjar, Abdullah ibn Sa'id, al-Qalanisi, and others where they permit two agents, one a creator and the other an acquirer, because they do not stipulate that creation subsist in the creator, and you have agreed with them, and they stipulate that the act which is acquisition subsist in the acquirer, and you have also agreed with them in that. And speech is a name for the specific acquisition like movement, blackness, and others, so the one described by it is the locus, not other. But in terms of the fact that speech is related to the power of the creator and the power of the acquirer, it does not differ from other acts, except that the one described by its specific name is the one in whom it subsists, as we established. And upon stopping at this exposition, it becomes clear that this is obfuscation and deception upon the weak. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 916

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by opponents who argue that if a single act could be attributed to two agents, then a single speech could be attributed to two speakers, which they consider absurd. The author first states that this objection does not apply to the Maturidi position because they do not claim that one and the same act is the act of both God and the servant in the same sense. Rather, what is an act of God is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, whereas what is an act of the servant is not an act of God in that same sense but rather is God's object of action (maf‘ūl). The word 'act' (fi‘l) is a general term that has sub-categories; an act can be attributed to God by virtue of its generic name and to the servant by virtue of its specific name. For example, if God creates the act of hitting (ḍarb) in the servant, that hitting is God's creation and also the servant's act under the generic name, but specifically it is the servant's hitting because it subsists in him. The author then notes that the objection also does not apply to the Ash‘aris (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari) and others who deny that one act is by two agents in the first place; for them, only God creates acts, and the servant's act is merely acquisition (kasb). The author then explains that in the case of acquisition, the attribute (such as movement or speech) subsists in the servant, so the servant is described by it (he is the one who moves, speaks, etc.), while God is described as the creator of that attribute. It is impossible for the same attribute to subsist in two loci. The opponents' argument from necessary movements and attributes is then addressed: in necessary movement, the creator is God and the moved is the locus (the body); similarly, blackness has God as its creator and the black object as its locus. The author then shows that the objection also does not apply to those like al-Najjar, Abdullah ibn Sa'id, and al-Qalanisi, because they do not require that creation (khalq) subsist in the creator, and they require that the act which is acquisition subsist in the acquirer. Thus, speech is a specific acquisition that subsists in the servant, but both God's power and the servant's power relate to it. The conclusion is that the objection is mere obfuscation.

Key Terms
فعل
فاعل
كسب
خلق
محل
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidis believe that one and the same act is simultaneously the act of God and the act of the servant in the same sense.
Correction: They hold that the act is attributed to God as creator and to the servant as the one in whom it subsists, which are different respects.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi refutation, how is the act attributed to both God and the servant?
A) The same act is simultaneously an act of God and an act of the servant.
B) Act is attributed to God as creator and to the servant as acquirer by different considerations.
C) Only God is the agent; the servant has no act at all.
D) The act is attributed to the servant as creator and to God as acquirer.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi refutation hinges on distinguishing between the generic name of an act (attributed to God as creator) and its specific name (attributed to the servant as locus), thereby avoiding the absurdity of one act being by two agents in the same sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
As you go through your daily actions—typing, walking, speaking—do you consciously acknowledge that each of these is both God's creation and your own acquisition? How would your sense of gratitude and responsibility shift if you held this distinction at the forefront of your mind?
?
Is there a sin or shortcoming you have been attributing entirely to your own weakness (forgetting God's role) or entirely to God's decree (absolving yourself)? How does this lesson's teaching about God as creator and you as locus compel you to repent without blame?
?
When you use your tongue to speak, do you consider that your speech is a specific type of act created by God and acquired by you? What would change in your conversations if you truly believed that every word you utter is simultaneously a divine creation and your personal responsibility?

The Mu'tazilite Doctrine of the Non-Existent as a Thing
Nasafi outlines the Mu'tazilite doctrine that the non-existent is a thing with attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite claim that the non-existent is a thing and how they attribute to it essence, substance, and accident before existence.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilites say the non-existent is a thing, making it an object of power and knowledge before creation.

This lesson introduces the Mu'tazilite position that the non-existent (ma'dum) is a thing (shay') with real attributes like essence, substance, and accident prior to existence. Nasafi describes their view as irrational and based on partisanship, and he notes the variety within their school.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Notice the key terms: المعدوم, الشيئية, القدرة.
This passage is from Imam Nasafi's critique.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Find the statement that the non-existent is a thing (شيء) and that it has attributes like عين, عرض, جوهر before existence.
3
Understand the implications
Consider why attributing thingness to non-existence matters for divine power and creation.
The next lesson will show the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضاً وموجودًا، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا.
We have explained that it is rational because rational proofs are established upon it, except that it is not imaginary. And if the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship, looked with reason, submitted to the proof, shunned desire, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are the ones saying what is not rational, holding onto what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of most of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity (ayn), an accident, a substance before coming into existence, similarly blackness, movement, and essence (dhat) according to what we have previously recorded in explaining their sayings. Then the power of the agent does not attach except to existence, and has no attachment to thingness (shay'iyya), and it does not become movement, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in preeternity. Then existence is not a meaning additional to the essence, and power has no attachment to the essence, so its attachment to existence is inconceivable since it is not a meaning additional to the essence. Thus power attaches to nothing, neither the eternal power nor the temporally originated power attaches to any object of power (maqdur) at all. In this is the nullification of the Maker, the statement of the preeternity of the world, the annulment of the establishment of action for servants, and the nullification of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And we say: God Almighty created the world and made what is not blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, or existence into blackness, whiteness, substance, accident and existence. Then whatever of that is the actions of servants, their existence and thingness are attached to the power of God Almighty, and their being movement, stillness, obedience, and disobedience are attached to the power of the servant. According to them, thingness is not attached to anyone's power, and existence is not a meaning additional to thingness, so it is necessary that the power of the servant does not attach to it, so they could not attach the power of the servant except to what we said.
Source pages p. 919

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that the non-existent (ma'dum) is a thing (shay') and that power (qudra) attaches only to existence. The author begins by stating that the issue is rationally clear, but the Mu'tazila are blinded by partisanship. He describes their doctrine: they claim the non-existent is a thing, and even assign to it attributes like being an entity, substance, or accident before existence. Then he argues that if power attaches only to existence, and existence is not additional to the essence, then power cannot attach to the essence either, leading to the conclusion that power attaches to nothing. This would nullify divine power entirely, implying preeternity of the world and negation of actions for servants. To counter this, the author states his own position: God creates the world and brings non-existent attributes into existence; for human actions, the existence and thingness depend on God's power while the specific quality (movement, stillness, obedience) depends on human power. The Mu'tazila, by denying thingness as an object of power, cannot consistently attribute any power to the servant except as the author has stated.

Key Terms
المعدوم
الشيئية
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazilite denial of attributes is purely philosophical without practical consequences.
Correction: Here it leads to a specific claim about non-existence that has implications for divine power, as shown in the next lesson.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do most Mu'tazilites claim about the non-existent?
A) It is absolutely nothing.
B) It is a thing with attributes like substance and accident before existence.
C) It is only an imaginary concept.
D) It is a creation of human minds.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites assert that the non-existent is a real thing with attributes, a claim that forms the basis for their theory of divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a belief simply because it was held by your group or sect, without honestly examining whether it aligns with clear reason and revelation? When will you commit to abandoning partisanship and seeking truth solely for Allah's sake?
?
The Mu'tazila allowed their desire to preserve God's oneness to lead them to claim that the non-existent is a thing with attributes. What desire in your own heart—perhaps for intellectual control or self-justification—might be blinding you to a truth about your relationship with your Creator?
?
If you truly believed that everything you think and do is witnessed by the One who creates all things, would you dare to hold a view about Him that contradicts His own words? How then will you respond when you encounter a doctrine like this that tests your submission?

Nasafi's Refutation and the True Nature of Divine and Human Power
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite view and presents the correct doctrine of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the Mu'tazilite view leads to the nullification of divine power and his alternative explanation of how power attaches to actions.

Core Idea
If power only attaches to existence, and existence is not additional to essence, then power attaches to nothing—nullifying all divine power.

In this lesson, Nasafi builds on the Mu'tazilite premise to show its absurd consequences. He argues that if power attaches only to existence and existence is not an additional attribute, then power can attach to nothing, which would nullify the Creator and imply the preeternity of the world. Then he presents the Ash'ari-Maturidi position: God creates the thingness and existence of all things, while the servant's power attaches to the specific qualities like movement and obedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic refutation
Read the Arabic passage from 'ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود' to the end. Identify Nasafi's logical steps.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi shows that if existence is not additional to essence, and power only attaches to existence, then power attaches to nothing. This leads to five consequences: nullification of Maker, preeternity of world, etc.
These consequences are listed.
3
Understand Nasafi's alternative
Read his positive statement: God creates existence and thingness; human power attaches to the specific characterization (being movement, obedience, etc.).
This resolves the problem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضاً وموجودًا، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا.
We have explained that it is rational because rational proofs are established upon it, except that it is not imaginary. And if the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship, looked with reason, submitted to the proof, shunned desire, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are the ones saying what is not rational, holding onto what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of most of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity (ayn), an accident, a substance before coming into existence, similarly blackness, movement, and essence (dhat) according to what we have previously recorded in explaining their sayings. Then the power of the agent does not attach except to existence, and has no attachment to thingness (shay'iyya), and it does not become movement, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in preeternity. Then existence is not a meaning additional to the essence, and power has no attachment to the essence, so its attachment to existence is inconceivable since it is not a meaning additional to the essence. Thus power attaches to nothing, neither the eternal power nor the temporally originated power attaches to any object of power (maqdur) at all. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite view that power attaches only to existence is harmless.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the consequence of the Mu'tazilite view that power attaches only to existence?
A) It affirms the world's creation in time.
B) It nullifies the Maker and implies the world's preeternity.
C) It proves human free will.
D) It establishes the reality of accidents.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi disproves the Mu'tazilite theory by showing it leads to the denial of all power, and he replaces it with a two-tiered account of divine and human causal roles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah creates the very existence of your actions, and only their moral quality is from you, does this humble you or make you more conscious of your accountability? How will you change your intention before each action starting today?
?
The passage shows that denying even one attribute of Allah can lead to nullifying all His power. Have you ever trivialized any of Allah's attributes in your mind? What will you do to guard your understanding of His names and attributes from this lesson?
?
If your power is limited only to the specific characterization of your actions (movement, stillness, etc.), are you tempted to feel that your choices are insignificant? Conversely, how does knowing that Allah gives existence to your choices encourage you to strive for obedience?

The Principle of Action: Creation and Acquisition
Nasafi presents the principle of action attribution using the example of movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi principle that a single action can be attributed to both Allah as Creator and to the human as Acquirer.

Core Idea
Actions are created by Allah and acquired by humans.

Before addressing the specific question of kufr, Nasafi establishes a foundational principle: when a movement involves both a Creator and a human agent, it is considered an act of both—Allah creates it and the human acquires it. This principle is essential for understanding how sinful actions can be attributed to humans without attributing evil to Allah. Read the passage to see how he illustrates this with the example of wind and movers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with attention to the example
The passage uses the example of wind and two movers. Notice how the same movement is described as both an act of Allah (praised) and an act of the human (blamed).
The principle is that attribution depends on the agent's role: creation vs. acquisition.
2
Identify the key distinction
Nasafi distinguishes between the act as creation (فعل الله) and as acquisition (فعل العبد). This distinction is central to Maturidi theology.
3
Apply the principle to the broader debate
Think about how this principle will be used to answer the objection about kufr. The principle allows that an evil act can be created by Allah (good in creation) but acquired by the human (evil in intention).
This prepares for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحد منهما عليها ويثاب ويذم العاصي منهما عليها ويعاقب، وكذا لو كان المحركين الريح كانت الحركة في نفسها فعلاً الله تعالى ويحمد عليه وفعلاً للمحرك المنهى عنه ومعصية منه يذم عليها ويعاقب، وإن لم تكن هي متجزئة في نفسها، والله الموفق. وبهذا يجابون عن قولهم: إن الكافر من فعله الكفر. قلنا: نحن نسلم هذا، ولكن عندنا الكفر فعل الكافر لا فعل الله تعالى وإنما هو مفعوله، ومن سلم لكم أن الكفر فعل الله تعالى من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث فإنهم يمنعون أن يكون الكافر من كان الكفر فعله ويقولون: الكافر من كان الكفر فعله، ويقولون: من قام به الكفر لا من فعل الكفر كما أن المتحرك من قامت به الحركة لا من فعل الحركة والميت من قام به الموت لا من فعل الموت، وكذا هذا في السواد والبياض والحرارة والبرودة والحلاوة والحموضة والطول والقصر، فإما ما تزعمون أن الميت المريض الطويل القصير الأسود الأبيض الحار البارد الحلو الحامض هو الله تعالى لكون هذه المعاني فعلاً له فتنسلخون عن الدين، وإما أن تقروا بتناقض مذهبكم وبطلان شبهتكم.
One of them is praised and the disobedient one of them is blamed and punished, and likewise if the movers of the wind: the movement in itself is an act of Allah, praised for it, and an act of the mover forbidden and a disobedience from him for which he is blamed and punished, even if it is not divisible in itself. And Allah is the grantor of success. And with this they answer their statement: 'The disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr.' We say: we accept this, but in our view kufr is the act of the disbeliever, not the act of Allah, rather it is His created thing. And whoever concedes to you that kufr is the act of Allah among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the People of Hadith, they prevent that the disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr, and they say: the disbeliever is the one from whom kufr proceeds, and they say: the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who does kufr, just as the moving thing is the one in which movement inheres, not the one who does movement, and the dead is the one in whom death inheres, not the one who does death. And likewise this applies to blackness, whiteness, heat, cold, sweetness, sourness, tallness, shortness. So either you claim that the dead, the sick, the tall, the short, the black, the white, the hot, the cold, the sweet, the sour is Allah because these meanings are His act, and then you divest yourselves of religion, or you admit the contradiction of your doctrine and the falsity of your argument.
Source pages p. 923

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. It begins by stating a principle: when two agents are involved in a movement (e.g., Allah as creator and the human as actor), the movement is considered an act of Allah in terms of creation (praised), and an act of the human in terms of acquisition (blamed if forbidden). Using this principle, the author answers the objection that the disbeliever is the one who does kufr. The Maturidis accept that kufr is the act of the disbeliever, but they clarify: kufr is the act of the disbeliever as acquisition (kasb), not as creation. The Najjariyya and some hadith scholars go further, arguing that names like 'disbeliever' refer to the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who creates it, analogous to 'moving' referring to the thing that moves, not the creator of movement. This leads to a dilemma: if attributes like tallness and sweetness are acts of Allah, then applying them to creatures would force the opponent to say Allah has those attributes, which is absurd. Thus the opponent's position is contradictory.

Key Terms
فعل
مفعول
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidis believe humans do not truly act; Allah does everything.
Correction: This passage shows that humans truly acquire actions, and are held responsible for them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the movement as an act of Allah and as an act of the human?
A) They are two different movements
B) They are the same movement considered from different perspectives
C) The human creates the movement
D) Allah does not create sinful actions

Key Takeaway
A single action can be attributed to Allah as Creator and to the human as Acquirer, explaining human responsibility without attributing evil to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever committed a sin and then blamed your circumstances or even Allah for it, forgetting that while Allah created the action, you acquired it? How does this principle change your accountability before Allah?
?
In what areas of your life do you need to take more ownership of your actions, knowing that you are the acquirer and will be held responsible?
?
How does knowing that disobedience is your own acquisition affect your repentance? Does it make you more humble or more desperate for Allah's mercy?

Answering the Objection: Kufr as the Act of the Disbeliever
Nasafi responds to the objection about kufr and introduces the Najjariyya view, culminating in a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidis respond to the objection that kufr is the act of the disbeliever, and the dilemma posed to the Najjariyya position.

Core Idea
Kufr is the disbeliever's act by acquisition, not creation.

Having established the principle of action attribution, Nasafi now applies it to the specific objection: 'The disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr.' He accepts this but clarifies the nature of the attribution. Then he presents a stronger view from the Najjariyya and Hadith scholars, leading to a powerful dilemma that exposes the contradiction in the opponents' argument. Read carefully to follow the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key claims
Nasafi accepts the objection's wording but redefines it. Note how he distinguishes between 'act' (فعل) and 'created thing' (مفعول).
2
Understand the Najjariyya position
The Najjariyya go further: they say 'disbeliever' refers to the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who creates it. They use analogies like movement and death.
This is a different theological school.
3
Analyse the dilemma
Nasafi presents a dilemma: either you say Allah is dead, sick, etc. (absurd), or you admit your argument is contradictory. Understand why this follows.
This refutation depends on the analogy.

Source Text

?

Creation of Evil is Not Evil
Nasafi begins to argue that creation of evil is not evil, citing lack of human origination power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the creation of evil is not itself evil, based on the premise that only Allah has the power of origination.

Core Idea
Creating evil is not evil because only Allah originates all things.

Nasafi addresses a profound theological question: If Allah creates all things, including evil acts, does that make Him evil? In this passage, he begins to argue that the creation of evil is not morally evil, because evil is a quality of the act itself, not of its creation. The key premise is that human beings lack the power to originate (ikhtira')—only Allah can bring something into existence from nothing. This foundational idea shapes the rest of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Pay attention to the key terms: إيجاد القبيح, السفه, الاختراع.
The passage is cut off mid-sentence, but the core argument is clear.
2
Identify the two proofs referenced
The passage refers to 'the two proofs' that the servant has an act but no power of origination. Understand the distinction between action (fi'l) and origination (ikhtira').
This distinction is crucial for the argument.
3
Trace the logical conclusion
From the premise that only Allah originates, Nasafi concludes that every event is His creation. Therefore, the creation of evil is not evil, because evil is a quality of the act itself, not of its creation.
The argument is incomplete, but the logical chain is clear from the given text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيجاد القبيح ليس بقبيح: وكذا من تمسك بالدليلين أعنى ما مر أن العبد له فعل وليست له قدرة الاختراع وعرف فساد قولهم إن إيجاد القبيح قبيح وإيجاد السفه سفه لأن الدليل الذي دل أن لا اختراع إلا من الله تعالى يوجب أن كل حادث كان باختراعه، وقيام
The creation of evil is not evil: And likewise, whoever adheres to the two proofs, namely what has passed that the servant has an act and does not have the power of origination (ikhtira'), and knows the corruption of their statement that the creation of evil is evil and the creation of foolishness is foolishness, because the proof that there is no origination except from Allah necessitates that every incident is by His origination, and the establishment...
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of an argument that creating evil is not itself evil. It references two proofs previously mentioned: that the servant has an act but not the power to originate (ikhtira'). Since only Allah can originate, and He creates everything, the act of creating evil is not evil; rather, evil is a description of the act itself, not of the creation of it. The text is incomplete, cutting off at 'and the establishment' (wa qiyam).

Key Terms
إيجاد القبيح
السفه
الاختراع
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah creates evil deeds, then He is evil.
Correction: Nasafi argues that creation of evil is not evil because evil is a moral quality of the act itself, not of its creation. Since only Allah originates, and He creates all acts, the act of creation is neutral; the moral quality belongs to the act's nature.

Checkpoint
What premise does Nasafi use to argue that creating evil is not evil?
A) The servant has no power to originate
B) Evil is defined by human intention
C) Allah does not create evil at all
D) Evil is only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument hinges on the distinction between the act of creation and the moral quality of the created act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you feel that you are the ultimate originator of that act, or do you recognize that Allah creates the act and you merely acquire it? How does this truth change your sense of pride or shame? Will you humbly repent and attribute both your good and bad actions to Allah's creation?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's creation of evil is not evil, then why do you still find yourself complaining about the evil in your life? Are you willing to stop accusing Allah of wrongdoing when you face hardship? This week, when a trial comes, will you say, 'This is from Allah, and it is not evil in itself'?
?
You often judge others' actions as evil. But do you ever think that Allah created that person's action, and yet the person is responsible because they performed it? How does this lesson make you more humble in judging others? Will you commit to withholding final judgment, since only Allah knows the full reality of creation?

Proof that God is Wise and Refutation of Mu'tazilites
Nasafi proves God's wisdom in all actions and refutes Mu'tazilite classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God is wise in all actions and how this refutes the Mu'tazilite misunderstanding of wisdom and foolishness.

Core Idea
God's wisdom encompasses all creation; human judgments of foolishness are limited.

Imam Nasafi presents a concise yet powerful argument for God's absolute wisdom. He begins by stating that the proof of God's wisdom entails that every created thing, whether judged good or evil by humans, is wise in purpose. This immediately challenges the Mu'tazilite assumption that some actions are foolish. In this lesson, we will unpack his reasoning and see why the Mu'tazilite position collapses under its own limited perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the assertive tone: the proof 'requires' something.
2
Identify the core claim
Nasafi states that God is wise in all He creates, regardless of human evaluation. What does this imply about Mu'tazilite categories?
3
Understand the refutation
The Mu'tazilites are said to be ignorant of true wisdom and foolishness because their intellects are deficient. Why is this a powerful critique?
4
Grasp the concluding point
The claim to know all divine wisdoms is falsified by intuition (البداهة). What does 'intuition' mean here?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل على كونه عز وجل حكيمًا يوجب أنه تعالى في جميع ما أوجده حكيم، قبيحاً كان ذلك الموجد أو حسنًا سفها كان أو حكمة، وعرف بذلك أن ما يظنه المعتزلة حكمًا وسفها ليس كما ظنوا ، وأنهم جاهلون بحقيقة الحكمة والسفه إذ الجهل عليهم جائز ممكن والخطأ على ما أقمنا من الدليل ممتنع ، والحاصل أنهم يحكمون بكون ما لا اطلاع لهم على وجه الحكمة بالسفه، وهذا جهل إذ عقولهم قاصرة عن كثير من الحكم البشرية، ودعوى الاطلاع على جميع الحكم الربوبية دعوى ظهر فسادها للبداهة، والله الموفق.
The proof that He, Might and Majestic, is wise requires that He, Exalted, is wise in all that He creates, whether that created thing is evil or good, foolishness or wisdom. And it is known by that that what the Mu'tazilites suppose to be wisdom and foolishness is not as they supposed, and that they are ignorant of the reality of wisdom and foolishness, since ignorance is possible and permissible for them, and error is impossible according to what we have established of proof. The upshot is that they judge that what they have no knowledge of its aspect of wisdom is foolishness, and this is ignorance, since their intellects are deficient with respect to many human wisdoms, and the claim of having knowledge of all divine wisdoms is a claim whose falsity is evident by intuition. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 925

Commentary
This passage is a proof of God's wisdom and a refutation of the Mu'tazilite misunderstanding. It begins by asserting that the proof that God is wise entails that He is wise in all created things, whether they appear good or evil, wise or foolish. Then it explains that this clarifies that the Mu'tazilite classification of things as wise or foolish is mistaken. They are ignorant of the true nature of wisdom and foolishness, and their judgment is flawed because it is possible for them to be ignorant and error is impossible from God. The passage concludes that the Mu'tazilites' claim to know all divine wisdoms is obviously false; human intellects are limited even with respect to human wisdoms.

Key Terms
حكيم
حكمة
سفه
قبيح
البداهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some actions of God appear pointless or evil, implying God may be foolish.
Correction: Nasafi argues that apparent foolishness is due to human ignorance; all divine actions are wise by definition, and it is impossible for God to act foolishly.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how does the Mu'tazilite claim to know all divine wisdoms stand?
A) It is evident by intuition.
B) Its falsity is evident by intuition.
C) It is supported by revealed texts.
D) It is a necessary truth.

Key Takeaway
God's wisdom covers all creation; human judgments of foolishness are a result of intellectual limitation, not divine imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness events in your life that seem unfair or pointless, do you secretly think God could have done better? What does this passage demand you to change?
?
The Mu'tazilites assumed they could judge God's actions. Where in your daily life do you similarly assume you know better than God's plan? What would it cost you to surrender that assumption?
?
Nasafi says even human wisdoms are beyond full grasp, let alone divine. How does this humility apply to your own judgments of others' actions? Will you now pause before labeling someone's act as foolish?
